Fard from Quran Cannot Be Performed as in Khabar Wahid
Usul principle on hierarchy of proofs for fard acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a fard established by a Qur'anic text cannot be performed in a manner specified solely by a khabar wahid, and apply it to a concrete fiqh scenario.

Core Idea
A fard from the Qur'an requires a qat'i proof for its manner; a single-narrator hadith cannot change it.

This passage from the Hidayah lays down a foundational usul principle about the hierarchy of proofs. It protects the certainty of a Qur'anic command from being modified by an uncertain report. In this lesson, we will parse the key terms and understand the legal reasoning behind this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two elements
The principle distinguishes between the obligation (fawdiyyah) and the manner (kayfiyyah) of an act. First, identify what act is being made fard and by what authority. Second, identify how that act is to be performed and by what authority.
2
Determine the authority of each element
The obligation comes from nass al-kitab (Qur'anic text), which is qat'i al-thubut. The manner comes from khabar wahid, which is zanni al-thubut. Recognize the epistemological weight: qat'i overrides zanni.
Hanafi usul distinguishes fard (qat'i) from wajib (zanni). Here, fard implies a higher level of certainty.
3
Apply the hierarchy
A zanni proof (khabar wahid) cannot modify a qat'i proof (Qur'an) in the essential manner of a fard. Therefore, if a khabar wahid prescribes a manner that contradicts or adds to the Qur'anic prescription for the fard, it is not binding for that aspect.
This does not mean the khabar wahid is rejected; it can be used for non-essential (sunnah) aspects.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
The principle applies only to the core manner of performing a fard. Khabar wahid can still inform other details like recommended acts (sunan) or conditions that do not alter the essence.
Example: The number of rak'ahs in salah is fard from Qur'an; a khabar wahid cannot change that number, but can specify a recommended du'a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ مَا ثَبَتَ فَوُضِيَّتُهُ بِنَصِ الْكِتَابِ لَا يَتَأَدَّى كَمَا ثَبَتَ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ.
Indeed, what is established in its obligation by a text of the Book (Qur'an) cannot be performed in the manner established by a single-narrator report (khabar wahid).
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This is a usul principle stating a hierarchy of authority in establishing both the obligation (wujub) of an act and its modality (kayfiyyah). If an act is made fard by a clear Qur'anic text (nass al-kitab, which is qat'i al-thubut and usually qat'i al-dalala), then the manner of its performance must also come from a source of at least equal authority. A khabar wahid (single-narrator hadith) is zanni al-thubut, so it cannot prescribe a different or additional method for performing that fard. However, this does not mean the khabar wahid is rejected entirely; it can be used for establishing sunan or non-core aspects. The principle guards against diluting the certainty of a Qur'anic command with an uncertain report.

Key Terms
فَوُضِيَّتُهُ (fawḍiyyatuhu): Its obligation (being made fard)
نَصِ الْكِتَابِ (naṣṣ al-kitāb): A clear textual statement from the Qur'an itself
خَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ (khabar al-wāḥid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle in this lesson, what is the ruling if a khabar wahid suggests a different posture for ruku' than what is commonly practiced?
A) The posture becomes wajib
B) The posture is considered sunnah, not fard
C) The fard of salah is invalidated without this posture
D) The khabar wahid abrogates the earlier practice

Key Takeaway
A fard from the Qur'an requires a qat'i proof for its essential manner; a khabar wahid cannot alter that essential modality.

Avoiding Harm to a Muslim is Wajib – Principle and Application
States a legal principle with proof and application to Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that avoiding harm to a Muslim is wajib, identify its proof from the hadith, and apply the priority rule that wajib overrides sunnah to the case of istilam during Hajj.

Core Idea
Avoiding harm to a Muslim is wajib; a wajib cannot be abandoned for a sunnah.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah establishes a core legal principle with a direct application to the Hajj ritual. The principle that avoiding harm to a Muslim is wajib is supported by the Prophet's ﷺ hadith. The passage then demonstrates how this principle governs the etiquette of kissing the Black Stone, showing that a higher obligation takes precedence over a recommended act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its ruling
Find the explicit statement: 'Avoiding harm to a Muslim is wajib.' Note that 'wajib' is a binding obligation in Hanafi fiqh, established by a zanni proof.
The principle is stated at the beginning of the extract.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith: 'A Muslim is one from whose tongue and hand other Muslims are safe.' Identify this as the primary evidence for the wajib ruling.
The hadith is narrated in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof establishes the ruling)
The hadith defines a Muslim as someone who does not harm others. This implies that avoiding harm is a necessary requirement of faith, making it wajib. The imperative to be safe from harm indicates an obligation to refrain from causing it.
Hanafi usul: general commands (awamir) indicate obligation unless specified otherwise.
4
Recognize the priority rule: wajib overrides sunnah
The text explicitly states: 'It is permissible to leave a sunnah for a wajib, but the opposite is not permissible.' This is a key legal maxim: a higher-ranking obligation cannot be sacrificed for a lower one.
This rule applies across all chapters of fiqh.
5
Apply the rule to the Hajj scenario (istilam)
Kissing the Black Stone (istilam) is sunnah. If trying to do so would cause harm to other Muslims (e.g., pushing in a crowd), then the wajib of avoiding harm takes precedence. The pilgrim should refrain and instead face the Stone and say takbir and tahlil.
This is a specific furu' case derived from the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۹۷ ) إِنَّ التَّحَرُّزَ عَنْ أذَى الْمُسْلِمِ وَاجِبٌ .
ترجمہ: مسلمان کو تکلیف پہنچانے سے بچنا واجب ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کسی مسلمان کو تکلیف واذیت دینے سے بچنا واجب ہے، اس لئے آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا الْمُسْلِمُ مَنْ سَلِمَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ مِنْ لِسَانِهِ وَيَدِهِ “
اور واجب کی وجہ سے سنت کا ترک جائز ہے لیکن اس کے برعکس سنت کی وجہ سے واجب کا ترک کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر حاجی کسی مسلمان کو اذیت دیے بغیر حجر اسود کو بوسہ دینے کی طاقت رکھتا ہے تو بوسہ دے ورنہ نہ دے، اس لئے کہ استلام حجر اسودسنت ہے اور مسلمان کو اذیت دینے سے بچنا واجب ہے اور سنت کی وجہ سے واجب کا ترک جائز نہیں ہے، لہذا ایسی صورت میں بوسہ کی جگہ دور سے استلام کرے۔

الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام ج ۱ ص ۲۲۰، ط: رحمانیه
إِنْ اسْتَطَعْتَ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ تُؤْذِى مُسْلِمًا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ لِعُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ إِنَّكَ رَجُلٌ أَيَّدْ تُؤْذِى الضَّعِيفَ فَلَا تُزَاحِمُ النَّاسَ عَلَى الْحَجَرِ، وَلَكِنْ إِنْ وَجَدْت فَرْجَةً فَاسْتَلِمُهُ، وَإِلَّا فَاسْتَقْبِلُهُ وَكَبِّرُ وَهَلَّلُ وَلَانَّ اسْتِلامَ الْحَجَرِ سُنَّةُ، وَالتَّحَرُّزَ عَنْ أَذَى الْمُسْلِمِ وَاجِبٌ فَلَا يَنْبَغِى لَهُ أَنْ يُؤْذِيَ مُسْلِمًا لِإِقَامَةِ السُّنَّةِ، وَلَكِنْ إِنْ اسْتَطَاعَ تَقْبِيلَهُ وَإِلَّا مَسَّ الْحَجَرَ بِيَدِهِ وَقَبَّلَ يَدَهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعُ ذَلِكَ أَمَسَّ الْحَجَرَ شَيْئًا مِنْ عُرْجُونِ أَوْ غَيْرِهِ، ثُمَّ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء جَاءَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ طَاقَ عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ، وَاسْتَلَمَ الْأَرْكَانَ بِمِحْجَنِهِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعُ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ اسْتَقْبَلَهُ وَكَبَّرَ وَهَلَّلَ وَحَمِدَ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى.
المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب المناسک ج۴ ص ۱۰، ط: دار المعرفة
الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، ج ۱ ص ۲۶۱، ط: رحمانيه
Indeed, avoiding the harm of a Muslim is obligatory. Translation: Avoiding causing pain to a Muslim is wajib. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that it is wajib to avoid causing pain and harm to any Muslim. For this reason, the Prophet ﷺ said: 'A Muslim is one from whose tongue and hand the Muslims are safe.' And it is permissible to leave a Sunnah for the sake of a Wajib, but the opposite – leaving a Wajib for the sake of a Sunnah – is not permissible. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to prove that if a pilgrim has the ability to kiss the Black Stone without harming any Muslim, he should kiss it; otherwise he should not. Because touching the Black Stone is Sunnah, and avoiding harm to a Muslim is Wajib, and leaving a Wajib for a Sunnah is not permissible. Therefore, in such a situation, he should gesture from a distance instead of kissing.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage introduces a foundational legal principle: avoiding harm to a Muslim is wajib (obligatory). The author supports this with the famous hadith: 'A Muslim is one from whose tongue and hand other Muslims are safe.' The commentary then explains that a wajib obligation can override a Sunnah (recommended) act, but a Sunnah cannot override a wajib. This is applied to the Hajj ritual of kissing the Black Stone. If a pilgrim can approach the Black Stone without causing harm to other Muslims, he should do so. However, if the crowd is dense and attempting to get close would cause harm, he must refrain because avoiding harm is wajib, while kissing the Stone is Sunnah. The text then quotes from al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut regarding the proper etiquette of istilam (touching the Stone) and emphasizes the priority of not harming others. The principle is clear: the higher obligation (wajib) takes precedence over a lesser one (sunnah).

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): obligatory; a legal category between fard and sunnah in Hanafi fiqh
سنة (sunnah): recommended act; omission is not sinful but contrary to ideal practice
استلام (istilam): touching or kissing the Black Stone during tawaf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in this lesson, what should a pilgrim do if approaching the Black Stone would cause harm to other Muslims?
A) Push through to kiss the Stone regardless.
B) Kiss the Stone using a stick from a distance.
C) Refrain from touching and face the Stone, saying takbir and tahlil.
D) Skip tawaf altogether.

Key Takeaway
Avoiding harm to a Muslim is a wajib that overrides any sunnah, such that if performing a recommended act causes harm, it must be abandoned.

Ruling Remains After Its Cause Disappears
Explains the Hanafi principle that a ruling persists after its cause is gone, with three examples from Hajj and Salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that a ruling established by a cause persists after the cause ceases and apply it to new examples from ibadat.

Core Idea
A ruling established by a cause remains after that cause disappears — the cause initiates, but does not sustain, the ruling.

This passage presents a fundamental Hanafi legal maxim: a ruling can outlive its original cause. The author illustrates this with three examples from Hajj and Salah: raml (brisk walking) in tawaf, stoning the Jamarat, and quiet recitation in Zuhr and Asr. Understanding this principle prevents the erroneous abandonment of established sunnahs when their historical circumstances no longer apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle and Examples
State the maxim: the ruling remains even if its cause is gone. Then list the three examples: raml, ramy, and quiet recitation.
2
Analyze Each Cause
For each example, identify the original cause: raml to show strength, ramy from Ibrahim's act, quiet recitation to avoid disturbance.
3
Understand Why the Ruling Remains
Explain that the cause is a sabab (initiator) not a shart (condition), so its removal does not nullify the ruling. The ruling becomes an independent sunnah.
Hanafis distinguish between sabab and shart.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Disagreement
Some Shafi'i and Maliki scholars argue that a ruling tied to a specific cause ceases when that cause ends. State the Hanafi position and its basis.
The disagreement is legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply to a New Example
Consider another ibadah practice that originated from a historical cause (e.g., the adhan for Jumu'ah). Apply the principle to determine whether it remains recommended.
Use the same logic: if the cause was merely the initiator, the ruling persists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باقی رہتا ہے اگر چہ سبب اب موجود نہ ہو، کیونکہ ایک چیز کے کئی اسباب ہو سکتے ہیں، لہذا کسی ایک سبب کے موجود نہ ہونے سے حکم بھی موجود نہ ہو ایسا نہیں ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ حاجی پہلے تین چکروں میں ریل کرے گا، یعنی اکٹر اکڑ کر چلے اور اس کا سبب یہ تھا کہ جب صحابہ کرام مکہ میں آئے تو مشرکین مکہ کہنے لگے کہ ان کو مدینے کی آب و ہوا نے کمزور کر دیا ہے ، تو آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے صحابہ کرام کو حکم دیا کہ اکثر کر چلیں تا کہ مشرکین کے سامنے بہادری اور طاقت ظاہر ہو جائے ، پھر یہ حکم آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانے میں بھی اور آپ کے بعد بھی اب تک باقی ہے، اگر چہ ابھی رمل کا سبب یعنی اظہارِ شجاعت و بہادری موجود نہیں لیکن چونکہ سبب کے زوال سے حکم زائل نہیں ہوتا، لہذا اب بھی یہ رمل کا حکم زائل نہ ہوگا، جیسے رمی جمار کا سبب حضرت ابراہیم علیہ السلام کا شیطان کو کنکریاں مارنا ہے، یہ سبب تو زائل ہو گیا لیکن حکم اب بھی باقی ہے۔ اسی طرح ظہر اور عصر کی نماز میں قرآت آہستہ پڑھنا اس لئے تھا کہ کفار قرآت کے دوران شور شرابہ کرتے تھے، مسلمانوں کو اذیت دیتے تھے،
اب یہ سب ختم ہو گیا لیکن حکم اب بھی باقی ہے۔
وَلَكِنَّهُ صَارَ سُنَّةٌ بِذَلِكَ السَّبَبِ فَيَبْقَى بَعْدَ زَوَالِهِ كَرَمُيِ الْحِمَارِ سَبَبُهُ رَمُئُ الْخَلِيلِ صَلَوَاتُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ الشَّيْطَانَ، ثُمَّ بَقِيَ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ ذَلِكَ السَّبَبِ.
المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب المناسک ج۴ ص ۱۰، ط: دار المعرفة
كَانَ سَبَبُهُ إِظْهَارَ الْجَلَدِ لِلْمُشْرِكِينَ حِينَ قَالُوا أَضْعَفَتُهُمْ حُمَّى يَشْرِبَ ثُمَّ بَقِيَ الْحُكْمُ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ السَّبَبِ كَالْإِخْفَاءِ فِي صَلَاةِ الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ كَانَ لِتَشْوِيشِ الْكَفَرَةِ وَأَذَاهُمُ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ عِنْدَ قِرَاء تِهِمُ الْقُرْآنَ فِي صَلَاتِهِمْ.
الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الحج، ج ا ص ۱۵۴، ط: المطبعة الخيرية
The ruling remains even if the cause is no longer present, because one thing can have multiple causes, so the absence of one cause does not necessitate the absence of the ruling. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that the pilgrim should perform raml in the first three rounds, i.e., walk with a brisk pace shaking their shoulders, and the reason for this was that when the Companions came to Makkah, the polytheists said that the climate of Madinah had weakened them, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered them to walk briskly to show bravery and strength before the polytheists. Then this ruling remained during the Prophet's time and after him until now, even though the cause of raml, i.e., displaying courage and bravery, no longer exists, but because the ruling does not cease with the cessation of the cause, therefore the ruling of raml will not cease. Similarly, the ruling of throwing pebbles at the Jamarat originated from Ibrahim (peace be upon him) throwing pebbles at Satan; that cause has gone, but the ruling remains. Likewise, reciting quietly in Zuhr and Asr prayers was because the disbelievers used to make noise and annoy the Muslims when they recited the Quran in their prayers; now that has ended, but the ruling remains. [Arabic texts: 'But it became a sunnah due to that cause, so it remains after its removal, like the throwing of pebbles at the Jamarat, whose cause was the Friend of Allah (peace be upon him) throwing at Satan, then it remained after the removal of that cause.' (al-Mabsut, vol. 4, p. 10) and 'Its cause was displaying vigor against the polytheists when they said "the fever of Yathrib has weakened them," then the ruling remained after the removal of the cause, like the quiet recitation in Zuhr and Asr was because of the disturbance by the disbelievers and their causing harm to the Muslims when they recited the Quran in their prayers.' (al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah, Hajj, vol. 1, p. 154)]
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental Hanafi legal maxim: a ruling established by a cause persists even after that cause ceases to exist. The author illustrates this with three examples from the Hajj and Salah rituals. First, the practice of raml (brisk walking) in the first three rounds of tawaf was originally prescribed to demonstrate physical strength to the pagan Quraysh who had claimed the Muslims were weakened by Madinah's climate. Although this display of bravado is no longer necessary, the sunnah of raml remains. Second, the stoning of the Jamarat (ramy) was originally performed by Prophet Ibrahim (peace be upon him) to repel Satan, and it remains a Hajj rite today even though that specific cause is gone. Third, the silent recitation in Zuhr and Asr prayers was instituted to avoid disturbance from the polytheists who would chant loudly to drown out the Quran recitation; that disturbance no longer exists, but quiet recitation remains. The supporting Arabic quotes from al-Mabsut and al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah confirm this principle.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): A cause or reason that initiates a ruling but is not necessarily a condition for its continuity.
حکم (hukm): A legal ruling or prescription (e.g., sunnah, wajib) established by the Lawgiver.
رمل (raml): A brisk walking style with shoulder-shaking performed during the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed, why does the sunnah of raml in tawaf remain today even though the original cause (showing strength to polytheists) no longer exists?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly commanded raml for all times regardless of cause.
B) Because a ruling established by a cause persists after the cause's removal unless the ruling was tied to the cause as a condition.
C) Because raml is a wajib act that cannot be abrogated.
D) Because the polytheists still exist today.

Key Takeaway
A sunnah established by a specific cause remains a sunnah even after that cause disappears.

The Analogy: Tawaf Circuits as Rak'ahs
Establishes the analogy between tawaf circuits and prayer rak'ahs, leading to starting each circuit with istilam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istilam for each tawaf circuit and explain the analogical reasoning from prayer rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Each circuit of tawaf is an independent unit like a rak'ah, so each begins with its own istilam.

This lesson introduces a key analogy in Hanafi fiqh: the circuits of tawaf are likened to the rak'ahs of prayer. Just as each rak'ah begins with the opening takbir, each circuit of tawaf begins with istilam (touching or pointing to the Black Stone). Understanding this analogy helps clarify the sunnah status of istilam for each circuit.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on istilam
Identify the ruling: it is sunnah to perform istilam at the beginning of each tawaf circuit. Note that this is the mufta bihi (relied upon) position.
The source explicitly states the analogy as the basis.
2
Identify the analogy used
The text says: 'Inna ashwata al-tawafi karaka'ati al-salah' — the circuits of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayer. Understand that this is a qiyas (analogical reasoning).
The word 'ka' (like) establishes the comparison.
3
Extract the proof from the source
The source quotes earlier works (al-Mabsut, al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah) that explain how a sunnah remains even after its original cause is gone. This reinforces the application of the analogy.
Refer to the dalil_block for the textual evidence.
4
Apply the analogy to each circuit
Conclude that just as each rak'ah has its own opening takbir, each shawt (circuit) has its own opening istilam. The ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
This is the core conclusion of the passage.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Note that Shafi'is consider istilam mustahab (recommended) rather than sunnah mu'akkadah. The practical difference is minimal but affects the emphasis in fiqh manuals.
See al-mukhtalaf_fih for details.

(۲۰۰) إِنَّ أَشْوَاطَ الطَّوَافِ كَرَكَعَاتِ الصَّلَاةِ.
ترجمہ: طواف کے چکر نماز کی رکعتوں کے مانند ہیں۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ طواف کے چکروں کی نماز کی رکعات کے ساتھ وَلَكِنَّهُ صَارَ سُنَّةٌ بِذَلِكَ السَّبَبِ فَيَبْقَى بَعْدَ زَوَالِهِ كَرَمُيِ الْحِمَارِ سَبَبُهُ رَمُئُ الْخَلِيلِ صَلَوَاتُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ الشَّيْطَانَ، ثُمَّ بَقِيَ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ ذَلِكَ السَّبَبِ.

الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الحج، ج ا ص ۱۵۴، ط: المطبعة الخيرية

(200) Verily, the circuits of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayer.
Translation: The rounds of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayer.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the rounds of tawaf are with respect to the rak'ahs of prayer, and [then the Arabic quote continues: 'But it became a sunnah due to that cause, so it remains after its removal, like the throwing of pebbles...' etc.]
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage introduces a key Hanafi analogy: the circuits (ashwat) of tawaf are likened to the rak'ahs of prayer. The commentator explains that just as each rak'ah of prayer is initiated with the takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar'), each circuit of tawaf should be initiated with the istilam (touching or pointing to) of the Black Stone. This analogy establishes that each tawaf round is an independent unit like a rak'ah, requiring its own opening act. The supporting Arabic quotes from al-Mabsut and al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah reiterate the principle that a ruling remains after its cause is gone, which here reinforces that the sunnah of istilam at the start of each circuit is established.

Key Terms
اشواط (ashwat): Circuits or rounds of tawaf around the Kaaba; each complete circle is one shawt.
ركعات (rak'at): Units of prayer, each consisting of standing, bowing, prostrating, etc.
استلام (istilam): The act of touching or kissing the Black Stone, or pointing to it if unable, at the start of each tawaf circuit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that istilam of the Black Stone is sunnah at the beginning of each circuit of tawaf?
A) Because the Prophet did it once and it became a general rule.
B) Because tawaf circuits are analogous to prayer rak'ahs, each of which begins with takbir.
C) Because each circuit is a separate act of worship requiring its own intention.
D) Because the Black Stone is considered a substitute for the Kaaba.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school analogizes tawaf circuits to prayer rak'ahs, making istilam at the start of each circuit a sunnah, not a one-time act.

Return to the Black Stone After Tawaf When Followed by Sa'y
Ruling with proof: principle and analogy for returning to Black Stone before sa'y.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for returning to the Black Stone after tawaf when sa'y follows, and explain its proof using the analogy to prayer rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Every tawaf followed by sa'y requires a return to the Black Stone so that sa'y begins with istilam.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key sequence in Hajj: when tawaf is followed by sa'y between Safa and Marwah, the pilgrim must return to the Black Stone for istilam after praying two rak'ahs. This ensures that sa'y, like tawaf, begins with istilam. The rule is rooted in an analogy to prayer, where each rak'ah begins with takbir. Understanding this principle helps avoid a common mistake that the two rak'ahs are the final step before sa'y.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the specific act: returning to the Black Stone after tawaf and before sa'y. The Hanafi school classifies this as sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
The ruling applies only to tawaf that is followed by sa'y (e.g., tawaf al-qudum, tawaf al-ifadah during Hajj, or any Umrah tawaf).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from al-Mabsut: the Prophet ﷺ instructed that whenever one passes the Black Stone during tawaf, one should touch it if possible. This establishes istilam at each circuit.
The hadith is about tawaf circuits, not directly about sa'y, but it serves as the basis for qiyas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy (qiyas) is explicit: tawaf circuits are like prayer rak'ahs. Just as each rak'ah begins with takbir, each circuit of tawaf begins with istilam. By extension, the entire sa'y (which follows tawaf) should also begin with istilam.
This is a clear analogical reasoning: the 'illa (effective cause) is the beginning of a ritual unit with a specific act.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not require this return; they consider the two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim as the culmination of tawaf, and sa'y begins directly from Safa without a final istilam.
This difference stems from a different view on the sequence and what marks the completion of tawaf.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that returning to the Black Stone is sunnah for tawaf followed by sa'y. This is supported by the analogy and confirmed in zahir al-riwayah texts.
Minor ikhtilaf exists within the Hanafi school (Ibn al-Humam considered it mustahabb), but the majority holds it as sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۰۱) إِنَّ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ سَعْيٌ يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ وَإِلَّا فَلَا.
ترجمہ: ہر وہ طواف جس کے بعد سعی ہو تو حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹے وگرنہ نہیں۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس طواف کے بعد سعی بین الصفا والمروۃ ہوگی تو اس طواف کے بعد حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹے گا، اور جس طواف کے بعد سعی نہ ہو تو پھر حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ طائف جب استلام کے ساتھ طواف کو ختم کرے گا، تو پھر مقام ابراہیم کی طرف آکر مقام ابراہیم پر یا جہاں آسان ہو مسجد میں دو رکعت پڑھے، پھر دوبارہ حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹ جائے اور حجر اسود کا استلام کرے، کیونکہ یہ ایسا طواف ہے کہ جس کے بعد سعی ہے اور ہر وہ طواف جس کے بعد سعی ہو تو اس میں حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹے گا، عود کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح استلام حجر کے ساتھ طواف کی ابتداء ہوتی ہے اسی طرح سعی کی ابتداء بھی اسی کے ساتھ ہو جائے۔
وَكُلَّمَا مَرَرْت بِالْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فِي طَوَافِكَ هَذَا فَاسْتَلِمُهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَعْت مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ تُؤْذِيَ مُسْلِمًا فَإِنْ لَمْ تَسْتَطِعْ فَاسْتَقْبِلُهُ وَكَبِّرُ وَهَلَّلُ، لِأَنَّ أَشْوَاطَ الطَّرَافِ كَرَكَعَاتِ الصَّلَوَاتِ فَكَمَا تَفْتَتِحُ كُلَّ رَكْعَةٍ تَقُومُ إِلَيْهَا بِالتَّكْبِيرِ فَكَذَلِكَ تَفْتَتِحُ كُلَّ شَوْطٍ بِاسْتِلَامِ الْحَجَرِ.
المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب المناسک ج۴ ص ا ا ، ط: دار المعرفة
الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، ج ۱ ص ۲۶۲، ط: رحمانیه
ثُمَّ يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فَيَسْتَلِمُهُ لِيَكُونَ افْتِتَاحُ السَّعْيِ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ بِاسْتِلَامِ الْحَجَرِ كَمَا يَكُونُ افْتِتَاحُ الطَّوَافِ بِاسْتِلَامِ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ، وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ =
(201) Verily, every tawaf after which there is sa'y should return to the Stone, otherwise not.
Translation: Every tawaf after which sa'y is performed should return to the Black Stone, otherwise not.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that for a tawaf after which sa'y between Safa and Marwah will be performed, after that tawaf one should return to the Black Stone, and for a tawaf after which there is no sa'y, there is no need to return to the Black Stone. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, explains that when the pilgrim completes the tawaf with istilam, he should then go to Maqam Ibrahim and pray two rak'ahs there or anywhere convenient in the mosque, then return again to the Black Stone and perform istilam of it, because this is a tawaf after which there is sa'y, and for every tawaf after which there is sa'y, one should return to the Black Stone. The reason for returning is that just as the tawaf begins with istilam of the Stone, so too the sa'y should begin with it. [Arabic: 'Whenever you pass by the Black Stone during this tawaf, if possible, touch it without harming a Muslim, and if not possible, face it and say takbir and tahlil, because the circuits of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayers; just as you begin every rak'ah you stand for with takbir, so you begin every circuit with istilam of the Stone.' (al-Mabsut) 'Then he returns to the Black Stone and touches it so that the start of sa'y between Safa and Marwah is with istilam of the Stone, just as the start of tawaf is with istilam of the Black Stone, and the principle is that every tawaf after which there is...' (cut off)]
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage outlines a specific rule for tawaf that is followed by sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah). The principle states: only if sa'y will follow should the pilgrim, after completing the tawaf and praying two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim, return to the Black Stone for a final istilam before proceeding to sa'y. This is because the sa'y should begin with istilam, just as the tawaf began with istilam. If the tawaf is not followed by sa'y (e.g., a voluntary tawaf or tawaf al-wada'), then no such return is necessary. The supporting text from al-Mabsut reinforces the analogy between tawaf circuits and prayer rak'ahs, and the practice of istilam at each pass. The al-Hidayah reference provides the source of the rule.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking seven times between the hills of Safa and Marwah as part of Hajj or Umrah.
حجر اسود (hajar al-aswad): The Black Stone set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba, used as a starting and ending marker for tawaf and sa'y.
عود ('awd): Returning to the Black Stone after completing the tawaf prayer, before beginning sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, after completing tawaf and praying two rak'ahs, what additional action is required (sunnah) before beginning sa'y?
A) Drink Zamzam water.
B) Return to the Black Stone and perform istilam.
C) Make supplication at the Multazam.
D) Go directly to Safa and begin sa'y.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, whenever sa'y follows tawaf, the pilgrim returns to the Black Stone for istilam to begin sa'y just as tawaf began, based on the analogy with prayer rak'ahs.

Returning to the Black Stone Before Sa'y
Establishes a principle with qiyas proof from al-Hidayah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that every tawaf followed by sa'y requires returning to the Black Stone, and explain the qiyas with prayer rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Each tawaf circuit mirrors a prayer rak'ah: both open with a formal act at the Black Stone.

In the Hajj rituals, the sequence of tawaf and sa'y has a specific order. This lesson from al-Hidayah establishes a key principle: whenever sa'y follows tawaf, the pilgrim must return to the Black Stone before starting sa'y. The analogy with prayer rak'ahs provides the legal reasoning, comparing each tawaf circuit to a rak'ah that begins with takbir.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the rule: 'Every tawaf after which there is sa'y, he returns to the Stone; otherwise not.' Identify the condition (tawaf with subsequent sa'y) and the required action (return to the Stone).
The principle distinguishes tawafs that are followed by sa'y from those that are not.
2
Identify the analogy
Find the text that compares tawaf circuits to prayer rak'ahs. Note the phrase 'لِأَنَّ أَشْوَاطَ الطَّرَافِ كَرَكَعَاتِ الصَّلَوَاتِ' (the circuits of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayers).
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (explicit analogy).
3
Trace the opening act
In prayer, each rak'ah opens with takbir; in tawaf, each circuit should open with touching (istilam) the Black Stone. Therefore, the sa'y, as a continuation of the worship, also opens with touching the Stone.
The return to the Stone after tawaf ensures that the start of sa'y mirrors the start of tawaf.
4
Apply the principle to different tawafs
Distinguish: tawaf al-qudum for a mutamatti' (followed by sa'y) requires return; tawaf al-wada' (not followed by sa'y) does not.
This practical application is crucial for performing Hajj correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ سَعُيِّ يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. تشبیہ ہے اور وجہ تشبیہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح نماز کی ہر رکعت کو تکبیر سے شروع کیا جاتا ہے، اسی طرح طواف کے بھی ہر چکر کو استلام حجر سے شروع کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ طواف کے ہر چکر کو استلام حجر سے شروع کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ طواف کے چکر نماز کی رکعات کی مانند ہیں اور نماز کی ہر رکعت تکبیر سے شروع کی جاتی ہے، لہذ اطواف کا بھی ہر چکر استلام حجر سے شروع کیا جائے گا۔ (۲۰۱) إِنَّ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ سَعُيِّ يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. ترجمہ: ہر وہ طواف جس کے بعد سعی ہو تو حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹے وگرنہ نہیں۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس طواف کے بعد سعی بین الصفا والمروۃ ہوگی تو اس طواف کے بعد حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹے گا، اور جس طواف کے بعد سعی نہ ہو تو پھر حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلارہے ہیں کہ طائف جب استلام کے ساتھ طواف کو ختم کرے گا، تو پھر مقام ابراہیم کی طرف آکر مقام ابراہیم پر یا جہاں آسان ہو مسجد میں دو رکعت پڑھے، پھر دوبارہ حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹ جائے اور حجر اسود کا استلام کرے، کیونکہ یہ ایسا طواف ہے کہ جس کے بعد سعی ہے اور ہر وہ طواف جس کے بعد سعی ہو تو اس میں حجر اسود کی طرف لوٹے گا، عود کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جس طرح استلام حجر کے ساتھ طواف کی ابتداء ہوتی ہے اسی طرح سعی کی ابتداء بھی اسی کے ساتھ ہو جائے۔ وَكُلَّمَا مَرَرْت بِالْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فِي طَوَافِكَ هَذَا فَاسْتَلِمُهُ إِنِ اسْتَطَعْت مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ تُؤْذِيَ مُسْلِمًا فَإِنْ لَمْ تَسْتَطِعْ فَاسْتَقْبِلُهُ وَكَبِّرُ وَهَلَّلُ، لِأَنَّ أَشْوَاطَ الطَّرَافِ كَرَكَعَاتِ الصَّلَوَاتِ فَكَمَا تَفْتَتِحُ كُلَّ رَكْعَةٍ تَقُومُ إِلَيْهَا بِالتَّكْبِيرِ فَكَذَلِكَ تَفْتَتِحُ كُلَّ شَوْطٍ بِاسْتِلَامِ الْحَجَرِ. المبسوط للسرخسی کتاب المناسک ج۴ ص ا ا ، ط: دار المعرفة الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، ج ۱ ص ۲۶۲، ط: رحمانیه ثُمَّ يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ فَيَسْتَلِمُهُ لِيَكُونَ افْتِتَاحُ السَّعْيِ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ بِاسْتِلَامِ الْحَجَرِ كَمَا يَكُونُ افْتِتَاحُ الطَّوَافِ بِاسْتِلَامِ الْحَجَرِ الْأَسْوَدِ، وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ كُلَّ طَوَافٍ بَعْدَهُ سَعْيٌ فَإِنَّهُ يَعُودُ بَعْدَ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ وَكُلُّ طَوَافٍ لَا سَعْيَ بَعْدَهُ لَا يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ.
Indeed, every tawaf after which there is sa'y, he returns to the Stone, and if not, then no. There is an analogy and the reason for the analogy is that just as every rak'ah of prayer is started with takbir, similarly every circuit of tawaf will be started with touching the Stone. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, proves that every circuit of tawaf will be started with touching the Stone, because the circuits of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayer, and every rak'ah of prayer is started with takbir, so every circuit of tawaf will be started with touching the Stone. (201) Indeed, every tawaf after which there is sa'y, he returns to the Stone, and if not, then no. Translation: Every tawaf after which there is sa'y, he returns to the Black Stone, otherwise not. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a tawaf after which there is sa'y between Safa and Marwah, after that tawaf he will return to the Black Stone, and a tawaf after which there is no sa'y, then there is no need to return to the Black Stone. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that when the one performing tawaf finishes tawaf with touching, then he goes to Maqam Ibrahim and prays two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim or wherever is easy in the mosque, then he returns again to the Black Stone and touches it, because this is a tawaf after which there is sa'y, and every tawaf after which there is sa'y, he returns to the Black Stone. The reason for returning is that just as the beginning of tawaf is with touching the Stone, similarly the beginning of sa'y is with it. And whenever you pass by the Black Stone in this tawaf of yours, touch it if you can without harming any Muslim, and if you cannot, then face it and say Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illallah, because the circuits of tawaf are like the rak'ahs of prayers, and just as you open every rak'ah you stand for with takbir, so you open every circuit with touching the Stone. Al-Mabsut li al-Sarakhsi, Kitab al-Manasik, vol. 4, p. 1 [؟], Dar al-Ma'rifah; al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Ihram, vol. 1, p. 262, Rahmaniyyah. Then he returns to the Black Stone and touches it so that the beginning of sa'y between Safa and Marwah is with touching the Stone just as the beginning of tawaf is with touching the Black Stone. The underlying principle is that every tawaf after which there is sa'y, he returns after prayer to the Stone, and every tawaf with no sa'y after it, he does not return to the Stone.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a legal principle (qa'idah) from al-Hidayah concerning the connection between tawaf and sa'y in Hajj and 'Umrah. The principle states: for any tawaf that is followed by sa'y (the walking between Safa and Marwah), the pilgrim must conclude the tawaf by returning to the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad) and touching it again before proceeding to sa'y. For tawafs that are not followed by sa'y (e.g., the tawaf al-qudum for someone who does not perform sa'y after it, or tawaf al-wada'), there is no need to return to the Stone. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the circuits (ashwat) of tawaf are analogous to the rak'ahs of prayer. Just as each rak'ah begins with the opening takbir, each circuit of tawaf should begin with an act of consecration at the Black Stone. Since the pilgrim begins the tawaf with touching the Stone, and the sa'y is a continuation of the worship sequence, the beginning of sa'y should also be marked by touching the Black Stone. Therefore, after completing the tawaf and the two rak'ahs, the pilgrim returns to the Stone, touches it, and then proceeds to sa'y. This ensures that both the tawaf and the sa'y commence with the same symbolic act. The passage includes a quotation from al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi, which provides a detailed description: whenever passing the Stone during tawaf, touch it if possible without harming others; otherwise face it and recite takbir and tahlil. The principle is supported by the analogy (qiyas) between tawaf circuits and prayer rak'ahs, both of which require a formal opening at each segment.

Key Terms
استلام حجر (istilam al-hajar): The act of touching or kissing the Black Stone as a mark of reverence.
سعي (sa'y): Walking seven times between the hills of Safa and Marwah.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah seven times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle mentioned, when must a pilgrim return to the Black Stone after completing tawaf?
A) After any tawaf, regardless of sa'y.
B) Only after tawaf al-ifadah.
C) After a tawaf that is followed by sa'y.
D) Only after tawaf al-qudum.

Key Takeaway
A tawaf that is followed by sa'y must be concluded by returning to the Black Stone, because both circuits and sa'y require an opening act analogous to the takbir in prayer.

Principle: A Pillar (Rukn) is Established Only by Definitive Evidence
A usul-al-fiqh principle applied to Hajj rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rukn and wajib based on the strength of evidence, and apply the principle to determine the category of an act in Hajj.

Core Idea
Rukn requires definitive proof; wajib can be established by probable evidence like a single-narrator hadith.

This passage from al-Hidayah introduces a key usuli principle that governs the classification of acts in worship. It explains that the status of being an integral pillar (rukn) can only be proven by evidence that yields certainty, while mere obligation (wajib) can be established by probable evidence. We will explore how this principle applies to tawaf and sa'y in Hajj, and to taharah in tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The passage states: 'Indeed, the status of being a pillar is established only by definitive evidence.' Recognize that rukniyyah requires dalil qat'i.
This is a foundational usul principle in Hanafi madhhab.
2
Apply to Sa'y
Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is proven by a khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report), which is zanni (probable). Therefore, sa'y is wajib, not rukn.
Omission of wajib requires dam (compensation) but Hajj remains valid.
3
Compare to Tawaf
Tawaf is proven by definitive text (nass) from the Quran, so it is a rukn (fard). Omission invalidates Hajj.
This contrast illustrates the consequence of evidence strength.
4
Extend to Taharah in Tawaf
Taharah (purity) during tawaf is established by khabar al-wahid, so it is wajib, not rukn. If omitted without excuse, dam is due.
Taharah is a condition (shart) for tawaf but not an integral part itself.
5
Understand the Consequence
Rukn omission invalidates the act (batil); wajib omission requires compensation but act is valid. This principle determines the legal weight of each component.
This difference affects fatwa and practice in Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الرُّكْنِيَّةَ لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلَّا بِدَلِيل مَقْطُوع بِهِ. ترجمه: رکنیت دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کسی شھی کارکن ہونا دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتا ہے، یعنی شئی کی رکنیت دلیل ظنی سے ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ سعی بین الصفا والمروة واجب ہے رکن نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ھی کی رکنیت دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور سعی بین الصفاء المروۃ دلیل ظنی سے ثابت ہے اس لئے واجب ہے فرض نہیں ہے۔ جس طرح طواف نص قطعی سے ثابت ہے اس لئے فرض ہے اور طہارت خبر واحد سے ثابت ہے اس لئے واجب ہے۔ لأنَّ الرُّكْنِيَّةَ لَا تَبتُ إِلَّا بِالنَّصَّ فَأَمَّا الْوُجُوبُ فَيَقْبتُ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ، لِأَنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْعَمَلَ وَلَا يُوجِبَ عِلْمَ الْيَقِينِ، وَالرُّكْنِيَّةُ إِنَّمَا تَثْبُتُ بِمَا يُوجِبُ عِلْمَ الْيَقِينِ فَأَصْلُ الطَّوَافِ رُكُنٌ ثَابِتٌ بِالنَّيِّ، وَالطَّهَارَةُ فِيهِ تَنْبُتُ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ فَيَكُونُ مُوجِبُ الْعَمَلِ دُونَ الْعِلْمِ فَلَمْ تَصِرُ الطَّهَارَةُ رُكْنًا، وَلَكِنَّهَا وَاجِبَةٌ. المبسوط للسرخسى كتاب الحج، باب الطواف، ج ۴ ص ۳۸، ط: دار المعرفة الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، ج ۱ ص ۲۶۴، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, the status of being a pillar (rukn) is established only by definitive evidence. Translation: Rukniyyah is established by definitive evidence. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that something being a pillar (rukn) is established by definitive evidence, that is, the pillarness of a thing is not established by probable evidence. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, informs that sa'y between Safa and Marwah is wajib, not a rukn, because rukniyyah is established by definitive evidence, and sa'y between Safa and Marwah is established by probable evidence, therefore it is wajib, not fard. Similarly, tawaf is established by definitive text, so it is fard, and taharah (purity) in tawaf is established by khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report), so it is wajib. Because rukniyyah is established only by text (nass); as for wujub (obligation), it is established by khabar al-wahid, because it necessitates action but does not necessitate certain knowledge. Rukniyyah is established only by that which necessitates certain knowledge. Thus, the original tawaf is a rukn established by the text, and taharah in it is established by khabar al-wahid, so it necessitates action without knowledge, so taharah does not become a rukn, but it is wajib. Al-Mabsut li al-Sarakhsi, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Tawaf, vol. 4, p. 38, Dar al-Ma'rifah; al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Ihram, vol. 1, p. 264, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational uṣūlī principle distinguishing between the categories of rukn (pillar), fard, and wajib. The principle states that a component of worship can be classified as a rukn (an integral part whose omission invalidates the act) only if it is established by a definitive proof (dalīl qaṭʿī), such as the clear text of the Quran or a mutawatir hadith. Obligations (wājib) that are not at the level of rukn can be established by probable proofs (dalīl ẓannī), such as a khabar al-wāḥid (single-narrator hadith). The author of al-Hidayah applies this principle to the acts of Hajj: tawaf is a rukn (fard) because it is proven by definitive evidence (the Quranic command), while saʿy between Safa and Marwah is wajib because its evidence is a khabar al-wāḥid. Similarly, the requirement of purity (ṭahārah) during tawaf is established by a single-narrator report, so it is wajib, not a rukn. The passage quotes from al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi, which explains the logic: khabar al-wāḥid produces action ('amal) but not certain knowledge ('ilm al-yaqīn), so it can establish wujūb but not rukniyyah. This principle is crucial for determining the legal weight of various acts in worship and their consequences if omitted.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): An integral part of an act of worship; omission invalidates the act entirely and requires repetition.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that is not a rukn; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.
خبر واحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few chains, not reaching tawatur; provides zanni evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is sa'y considered wajib and not a rukn according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because it is established by a khabar al-wahid, which provides probable evidence.
C) Because it is performed after tawaf.
D) Because it is a sunnah of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
A component of worship is a rukn only if proven by definitive evidence; if proven by probable evidence, it is a wajib whose omission requires compensation.

Principle: Sa'y Cannot Be Performed as Nafl
Clarifies that sa'y is only prescribed as an obligatory act, not as a voluntary one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why sa'y cannot be performed as a voluntary (nafl) act and apply this principle in the context of multiple tawafs.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib, not nafl—performing it voluntarily is invalid.

This lesson clarifies a fundamental principle in the fiqh of Hajj: sa'y is only prescribed when it is part of the obligatory rites of Hajj or 'Umrah. Unlike tawaf, which can be performed as nafl at any time, sa'y has no independent voluntary existence. Understanding this distinction prevents innovation in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal nature of sa'y
Determine whether sa'y is classified as wajib, sunnah, or nafl in the Hanafi school. The passage states it is not prescribed as nafl.
The Arabic phrase 'إِنَّ التَنَفَّلَ بِالسَّعي غَيْرُ مَشْرُوع' directly indicates this.
2
Contrast sa'y with tawaf
Recognize that tawaf can be performed as nafl, but sa'y is inherently linked to the Hajj/Umrah sequence.
Tawaf is a general act of worship; sa'y is specifically wajib in the rites.
3
Apply the principle to scenarios
For example, if a pilgrim performs multiple nafl tawafs, should he perform sa'y after each? The principle says no, because sa'y after a nafl tawaf is not prescribed.
Only the sa'y of the obligatory Hajj/Umrah tawaf is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ التَنَفَّلَ بِالسَّعي غَيْرُ مَشْرُوع. ترجمہ نفل سعی کرنا مشروع نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ سعی کا نفل ہونا مشروع نہیں ہے بلکہ شریعت میں سعی کا وجوب ثابت ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ طواف کرنے والا بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے گا جب بھی اسے موقع ملے لیکن ان طوافوں کے بعد سعی نہیں کرے گا، کیونکہ حج کے احرام =سَعُيٌّ فَإِنَّهُ يَعُودُ بَعْدَ الصَّلَاةِ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ وَكُلُّ طَوَافٍ لَا سَعْيَ بَعْدَهُ لَا يَعُودُ إِلَى الْحَجَرِ. بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الحج، فصل بیان سنن الحج، ج ۲ ص ۱۴۸، ط: دار الكتب العلمية الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام ج ۱ ص ۲۶۴، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, performing sa'y voluntarily is not prescribed. Translation: Performing sa'y as nafl is not prescribed. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that sa'y being nafl is not prescribed; rather, in Shari'ah, the obligation (wujub) of sa'y is established. The author of al-Hidayah, after mentioning this principle, states that the one performing tawaf will perform tawaf of the Ka'bah whenever he gets the opportunity, but he will not perform sa'y after these tawafs, because the ihram of Hajj = sa'y. Then he returns after prayer to the Stone, and every tawaf with no sa'y after it, he does not return to the Stone. Bada'i' al-Sana'i': Kitab al-Hajj, Fasl Bayan Sunan al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 148, Dar al-Kutub al-'Ilmiyyah; al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Ihram, vol. 1, p. 264, Rahmaniyyah.

Commentary
This passage states the principle that sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah) cannot be performed as a voluntary (nafl) act. Sa'y is inherently an obligatory act (wajib) tied to Hajj or 'Umrah; it is not an independent act of worship that one can perform at will. Therefore, if a person performs multiple tawafs (e.g., nafl tawaf) during his stay in Makkah, he should not perform sa'y after each one. Sa'y is only performed after the obligatory tawaf that is part of the Hajj or 'Umrah rites. The author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to explain that after a nafl tawaf, the pilgrim does not return to the Black Stone to begin sa'y, because sa'y is not prescribed for that tawaf. The passage references Bada'i' al-Sana'i' and al-Hidayah for support. The underlying logic is that sa'y is only prescribed when it is part of the sequence of Hajj or 'Umrah rites, which begin with ihram. A nafl tawaf is not preceded by ihram for Hajj/Umrah, so sa'y is not relevant.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): A voluntary act of worship, not obligatory.
سعي (sa'y): Walking between Safa and Marwah seven times, wajib in Hajj and 'Umrah.
مشروع (mashru'): Legislated, prescribed by Shari'ah.

Key Takeaway

intermediate
8 min
No Supererogatory Sa'y (Nafl) Is Prescribed
States that performing Sa'y as nafl is not legislated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that nafl Sa'y is not prescribed and explain the principle that acts of worship are confined to their textual basis and cannot be extended by analogy.

Core Idea
Sa'y is prescribed only once by text; analogy cannot create a second Sa'y.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that while nafl Tawaf is permissible, nafl Sa'y is not. The author addresses a potential analogy and explains why Sa'y is restricted to its textual occurrence. This distinction is rooted in the Hanafi methodology of confining acts of worship to explicit textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is performing Sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah) as a supererogatory (nafl) act. The ruling is that this is not prescribed (ghayr mashru').
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The proof is the absence of textual evidence (nass) for performing Sa'y more than once. The author states: 'لعدم ورود النص به' (due to lack of textual evidence for it).
This is a dalil 'adam (evidence of absence) - the lack of permission indicates prohibition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof establishes the ruling)
Since Sa'y is an act of worship ('ibadah), it is established solely by textual proof, not by analogy. The text (Qur'an and Hadith) prescribes Sa'y only once per Hajj/Umrah. Therefore, performing it extra is not legislated because there is no textual basis.
The Hanafi principle: al-‘ibadat mabniyyah ‘ala al-tawqif (acts of worship are based on divine instruction, not analogy).
4
Note the ikhtilaf (the opposing argument)
An objection is raised: since Sa'y follows Tawaf (al-sa'y taba' al-tawaf), and nafl Tawaf is permitted, then nafl Sa'y should also be permitted as a follower.
This is an argument by qiyas (analogy) from Tawaf to Sa'y.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (why the Hanafi view prevails)
The Hanafi response: Sa'y is established as an act of worship by text, not by qiyas. Therefore, it is confined to the text. The text came for doing it once (al-nass warada bi al-i'tiyan marratan), so performing it a second time by analogy is not valid because there is no place (mahall) for it – i.e., the original text does not leave room for extension by analogy.
This refutes the qiyas by showing that the relationship of 'following' (taba'iyyah) applies only to order, not to extending the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ التَنَفَّلَ بِالسَّعي غَيْرُ مَشْرُوع. ترجمہ نفل سعی کرنا مشروع نہیں ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ سعی کا نفل ہونا مشروع نہیں ہے بلکہ شریعت میں سعی کا وجوب ثابت ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ طواف کرنے والا بیت اللہ کا طواف کرے گا جب بھی اسے موقع ملے لیکن ان طوافوں کے بعد سعی نہیں کرے گا، کیونکہ حج کے احرام میں صرف ایک بار سعی واجب ہوتی ہے، اور وہ شخص طواف قدوم کے بعد سعی کر چکا ہے، اس لئے اب سعی کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے، اور ایسا بھی نہیں ہوسکتا کہ وہ شخص نفل سعی کرے، کیونکہ نفل سعی مشروع نہیں ہے۔ والتنفل بالسعى غير مشروع لعدم ورود النص به. فإن قلت : السعى تبع الطواف، ولهذا لا يجوز قبله والتنفل بمتبوعه مشروع فيجب أن يكون التنفل بالسعى أيضاً مشروعاً تبعاً للطواف . قلت : السعى إنما ثبت كونه عبادة بالنص، بخلاف القياس فيقتصر على النص، والنص ورد بالإتيان مرة فلا يشرع ثانياً بالقياس لأنه لا محل له. [البناية: كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، ج ۴، ص ۲۱۰، ط: دار الكتب العلمية الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، جا ص ۲۷۴، ط: رحمانیه
Indeed, performing supererogatory (nafl) Sa'y is not legislated. Translation: Doing nafl Sa'y is not prescribed. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that performing Sa'y as nafl is not prescribed; rather in the Shari'ah, the obligation (wujub) of Sa'y is established. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that a person performing Tawaf around the Ka'bah may do Tawaf whenever he gets an opportunity, but after those Tawafs he will not perform Sa'y, because in the Hajj state (ihram) only one Sa'y is obligatory, and that person has already performed Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum, so there is no need to perform Sa'y again. And it is not possible that he performs nafl Sa'y, because nafl Sa'y is not legislated. And performing nafl Sa'y is not legislated due to lack of textual evidence for it. If it is said: Sa'y follows Tawaf, therefore it is not allowed before it, and performing nafl of that which is followed (Tawaf) is legislated, so performing nafl of Sa'y should also be legislated as a follower of Tawaf. I say: Sa'y is only established as an act of worship by text, contrary to analogy, so it is confined to the text. And the text came for doing it once, so it is not legislated a second time by analogy because there is no place for it.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that performing Sa'y as a nafl (supererogatory) act is not prescribed in the Shari'ah. The commentator explains that Sa'y is wajib only once during the Hajj (after the initial Tawaf al-Qudum or Tawaf al-Ifadah). If a person performs multiple Tawafs (which are permissible as nafl), he should not perform Sa'y after them. Some might argue by analogy: since Tawaf can be performed as nafl, and Sa'y is a follower (tab') of Tawaf, then nafl Sa'y should also be allowed. The Hanafi response is that Sa'y is an act of worship established solely by textual proof (nas), not by analogy (qiyas). The text only prescribes Sa'y once, and analogy cannot extend it. Therefore, nafl Sa'y is not allowed. This guards against the misconception that any voluntary Tawaf justifies a voluntary Sa'y.

Key Terms
التنفل بالسعي (al-tanafful bil-sa'y): Performing Sa'y voluntarily (supererogatory) beyond the obligatory one.
مشروع (mashru'): Legislated or prescribed in the Shari'ah.
التبع (al-taba'): That which follows another (here: Sa'y follows Tawaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is performing additional Sa'y (nafl) after multiple Tawafs not allowed according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because Sa'y is not a valid act of worship if performed without Tawaf.
B) Because Sa'y is established by text only once, and analogy cannot expand it.
C) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade performing Sa'y outside of Hajj.
D) Because Sa'y is wajib, so nafl is not possible.

Key Takeaway
The extra Sa'y is not legislated because Sa'y is an act of worship established only by text (nas), and the text prescribes it once; analogy cannot create a new act of worship.

Standing (Wuquf) After Peltings That Are Followed by Another Pelting
States the rule on whether to pause after pelting each Jamarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for standing after each Jamarah and apply it to the Hajj ritual.

Core Idea
Stand after pelting only if another pelting follows; no stand after the last Jamarah.

During Hajj, the pilgrim performs the pelting of the Jamarat in sequence. A common question is whether to pause after each set of throws. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi rule: standing is a recommended practice (sunnah) only after those Jamarat that are followed by another pelting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sequence
Recognize that ramy (pelting) is performed at three Jamarat: Ula (first), Wusta (middle), and Aqabah (last).
The sequence matters: after Ula comes Wusta, after Wusta comes Aqabah, and after Aqabah there is no pelting.
2
Determine the ruling on standing
The Hanafi school classifies wuquf (standing) after ramy as sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.
This is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.
3
Apply the condition: 'another pelting follows'
Stand only if after your current ramy there is another ramy to be performed on the same day. This applies to the Ula and Wusta.
The text says: 'Every ramy after which there is a ramy, he stands; if not, then not.'
4
Identify the exception
After Jamarah al-Aqabah, no further pelting follows, so the pilgrim does not stand.
This is the direct application of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ كُلَّ رَمُي بَعْدَهُ رَمُنٌ يَقِفُ وَإِلَّا فَلَا. ترجمہ: ہر ایسی رمی جس کے بعد رمی ہو تو وقوف کرے وگرنہ نہیں۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ہر ایسی رمی یعنی کنکری پھینکنا جس کے بعد دوبارہ رمی ہو تو اس صورت میں رمی کے بعد وقوف کرے گا یعنی تھوڑی دیر رک جائے، جیسے جمرہ اولی کی رمی اور جمرہ اوسط کی رمی، اور اگر رمی کے بعد دوسری رمی نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں رمی کے بعد نہ ٹھہرے، جیسے جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ رمی کی ابتداء کرے گا اس مقام سے جو مسجد حیف کے ساتھ متصل ہے، پھر رمی کرے گا، ہر کنکری کے ساتھ تکبیر پڑھے اور اس رمی کے بعد ٹھہر جائے، پھر رمی کرے اسی مقام سے جس سے پہلے رمی کر چکا ہے اور اس کے بعد بھی ٹھہر جائے پھر جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے اور اس کے بعد نہ ٹھہرے، کیونکہ پہلے یعنی جمرہ اولی اور جمرہ اوسط کے بعد رمی ہے ، اور ہر وہ رمی جس کے رمی ہو تو وہاں وقوف کرے، تو لہذ اجمرہ اولی اور جمرہ اوسط کے ہاں بھی وقوف کرے گا اور جمرہ عقبہ کے بعد چونکہ رمی نہیں ہے اور ہر وہ رمی جس کے بعد رمی نہ ہو تو وقوف نہیں کرے گا، لہذ اجمرہ عقبہ کے بعد بھی وقوف نہ کرے۔ والأصل أن كل رمي بعده رمي وقف عنده وكل رمي ليس بعده رمي لم يقف عنده ورميه راكبا=
Indeed, every pelting after which there is a pelting, he stands, and if not, then not. Translation: Every such ramy after which there is another ramy, he should do wuquf (stand), otherwise not. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that for every such ramy (pelting stones) after which there is another ramy, he should stand after the ramy for a little while, like the pelting of the first Jamarah and the middle Jamarah. And if after the ramy there is no second ramy, then he should not stand, like the pelting of the Jamarah al-Aqabah. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that he will begin the pelting from the place adjacent to Masjid al-Khayf, then he will pelt, saying Takbir with each stone, and will stand after this pelting. Then he will pelt again from the same place he pelted before, and will also stand after it. Then he will pelt the Jamarah al-Aqabah and will not stand after it, because after the first and middle Jamarah there is another pelting, and every pelting after which there is a pelting, he will stand there. So he will stand at the first and middle Jamarah. And since after Jamarah al-Aqabah there is no pelting, and every pelting after which there is no pelting, he will not stand, so he will not stand after Jamarah al-Aqabah. And the principle is that every ramy after which there is ramy, he stands at it, and every ramy after which there is no ramy, he does not stand at it, and his pelting while riding...
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement without explicit proof. It establishes a practical rule for the pelting (ramy) of the Jamarat during Hajj. The rule: after pelting the first Jamarah (Jamarah Ula) and the middle Jamarah (Jamarah Wusta), the pilgrim should pause (stand) for a while because another pelting (the next Jamarah) follows. However, after pelting the Jamarah al-Aqabah, no pause is needed because no further pelting follows. The commentator explains this in detail, noting that the pilgrim should begin pelting from the area adjacent to Masjid al-Khayf (in Mina), say Takbir with each stone, and then pause. This pattern is repeated for the first two Jamarat, but not for the last. The original matn from Hidayah states the same rule. This lesson ensures the correct performance of ramy, distinguishing between the middle and final Jamarat.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles (stones) at the Jamarat during Hajj.
وقوف (wuquf): Standing or pausing after pelting, considered a recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Jamarah Wusta (middle)
C) Jamarah Aqabah (last)
D) All three

Key Takeaway
The rule for standing after pelting is simple: stand after each Jamarah only if another pelting follows; after the last, do not stand.

Principle: Non-Hajj Actions Omission No Dam
States a Hanafi principle and its application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding omission of non-Hajj actions and explain the practical consequence of the dispute over staying at Mina.

Core Idea
Only omission of an actual Hajj action requires dam; staying at Mina is not such an action.

This passage establishes a key Hanafi principle that distinguishes between actions that are part of Hajj and those that are merely facilitative. This principle directly affects whether a pilgrim must offer a compensatory sacrifice (dam). The author of Hidayah uses this principle to argue that intentionally staying outside Mina does not incur a dam, contrary to the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Locate the core statement: 'What is not from the actions of Hajj, its omission does not necessitate the jabir.' Recognize that this is the foundational rule being taught.
2
Understand the scope
The principle applies only to acts that are not defined as 'af'al al-hajj'. Acts like ihram, wuquf, tawaf, sa'y, and rami are considered actions of Hajj; other acts are not.
Hanafi school limits 'af'al al-hajj' to those explicitly defined by texts.
3
Apply to the case of staying at Mina
The author argues that staying at Mina is facilitative (to enable rami), not an independent Hajj act, so omitting it does not trigger a dam.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i considers staying at Mina wajib based on the Prophet's practice and Umar's instruction, thus its omission requires a dam.
5
Determine practical consequence
For a Hanafi pilgrim, intentionally spending the night outside Mina incurs no dam; for a Shafi'i pilgrim, it would require a dam.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۰۵) مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ أَفْعَالِ الْحَجَّ فَتَرُكُهُ لَا يُوجِبُ الْجَابِرَ .
ترجمہ: جو چیز حج کے افعال میں سے نہیں ہے اس کا ترک کرنا نقصان کو ثابت نہیں کرتا۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو فعل حج کے افعال میں سے نہ ہو اگر اس کو آدمی چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوتا، کیونکہ دم افعال حج کے کسی فعل کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے آتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی حاجی نے منی کے علاوہ کسی دوسری جگہ جان بوجھ کر رات گزاری تو ہمارے یہاں اس پر دم وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ قیام منی کا ثبوت اس لئے ہے تا کہ حاجی کے لئے رمی کرنا آسان ہو ، لہذا قیام منی افعال حج میں سے نہیں ہو گا اور اس کے ترک پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہوگی جو جبر نقصان کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہے یعنی دم وغیرہ۔ اس کے برخلاف امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے یہاں چونکہ قیام منی واجب ہے، لہذا اس کے ترک پر دم واجب ہوگا۔
(205) What is not from the actions of Hajj, its omission does not necessitate the compensator (jabir). Translation: Something that is not among the actions of Hajj, its omission does not prove a deficiency. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if a person omits an act that is not among the actions of Hajj, then no dam etc. is obligatory upon him, because dam comes due to omitting some action of Hajj. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning the above principle, is explaining that if a pilgrim intentionally spends the night at a place other than Mina, then according to us no dam etc. is obligatory upon him, because staying at Mina is established so that it becomes easy for the pilgrim to do rami in its days, so staying at Mina is not among the actions of Hajj, and its omission does not necessitate anything that is placed for compensating a deficiency, i.e., dam etc. In contrast, according to Imam Shafi'i, since staying at Mina is obligatory, so upon its omission dam becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the status of staying overnight at Mina during the days of Tashriq. The principle is that only omission of an actual action of Hajj (like standing at Arafat, tawaf, sa'y, rami) requires a compensatory offering (dam). Staying at Mina is not considered an action of Hajj; it is merely a facility to assist with pelting. Therefore, if a pilgrim intentionally spends the night elsewhere, no dam is required. The commentary contrasts this with the Shafi'i view, where staying at Mina is wajib and its omission necessitates dam. This is a useful example of how the Hanafi school determines what constitutes 'af'al al-hajj' (actions of Hajj) based on the underlying purpose (ta'lil).

Key Terms
أَفْعَال الْحَجّ (af'al al-hajj): The specific ritual actions that constitute the Hajj pilgrimage, such as ihram, standing at Arafat, tawaf, sa'y, rami, etc.
جَابِر (jabir): A compensatory offering (like dam) that repairs a deficiency in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must offer a dam
B) He commits a sin but no compensation
C) Nothing is required
D) He must repeat Hajj

Key Takeaway
Only omission of an actual action of Hajj necessitates dam; staying at Mina is not such an action.

Rukn Must Exist in Any Form
States that a rukn must be fulfilled regardless of manner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding the rukn and apply it to determine the validity of acts of worship.

Core Idea
A rukn's essence suffices; its specific manner does not affect validity.

This lesson explores a foundational principle from the Hanafi school: a rukn (pillar) of an act of worship must exist in its essence, regardless of how it is performed. The source underscores that the mere occurrence of the rukn is sufficient; variations in form or condition do not invalidate it. For instance, standing at Arafat during Hajj is a rukn; whether one stands while riding or standing on foot, the rukn is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the Arabic maxim: 'إِنَّ مَا هُوَ رُكْنٌ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ وُجُودِهِ كَيْفَمَا كَانَ'. Understand that it asserts the necessity of a rukn's existence in any manner.
2
Define 'rukn' in Hanafi fiqh
Recall that a rukn is an integral part of an act of worship; its omission renders the act invalid (bāṭil). Unlike wājib, a rukn cannot be compensated (e.g., by dam).
Hanafi school distinguishes between rukn and wājib; rukn must be present in essence.
3
Apply the principle to a Hajj ritual
Consider wuqūf at Arafat. The principle states that as long as the pilgrim is present at Arafat for any duration (even momentarily) and in any state (e.g., riding, walking, sick), the rukn is fulfilled.
The example is directly from the commentary: standing at Arafat while riding is valid.
4
Distinguish from non-rukns
Note that other acts of Hajj, such as spending the nights in Mina, are not rukn but wājib or sunnah. Their omission does not invalidate Hajj and may require compensation or none at all.
The source mentions that leaving Mina intentionally requires no dam, as it is not from the actions of Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۰۶) إِنَّ مَا هُوَ رُكُنْ لَا بُدَّ مِنْ وُجُودِهِ كَيْفَمَا كَانَ.
ترجمہ : جوشی رکن ہو اس کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے جس طرح بھی ہو۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز رکن ہو اس کا صرف پایا جانا ضروری ہے،اب اس کا پایا جانا جس طرح بھی ہو ، جس حالت میں بھی ہو۔

الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام ج ا ص ۱۲۱، ط: المطبعة الخيرية

(206) Indeed, whatever is a rukn, its existence is necessary in whatever way it may be. Translation: Something that is a rukn, its existence is necessary no matter how it is. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that whatever is a rukn, its mere existence is necessary, no matter how it exists, in whatever condition. = It is more virtuous for what we have narrated, and the principle regarding it is that every rami after which there is a rami, it is more virtuous to do it riding, otherwise walking. (Then citations from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and Al-Hidayah) And it is disliked to spend the nights of Mina except in Mina, and 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to discipline for leaving staying there. Commentary
The main principle is a foundational legal maxim: if an act is a rukn (pillar) of any act of worship, it must be fulfilled; the specific manner or condition of fulfillment is not critical as long as the essence exists. For example, in Hajj, standing at Arafat is a rukn; if one stands, even briefly or while riding, the rukn is valid. The additional texts included after the main commentary relate to other rulings: one about the virtue of pelting while riding (which clarifies that for jamarat where subsequent pelting exists, riding is superior), and a repetition of the ruling on staying in Mina (already covered in the previous lesson), reaffirming that it is not a rukn and no dam is required for omission. The inclusion of these notes serves to illustrate how the principle of rukn applies specifically to actions like rami and staying in Mina.

Key Terms
رُكْن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act of worship; its omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must repeat the standing on foot
D) He must offer a sacrifice

Key Takeaway
A rukn of any worship must be present in its essence; the specific form or condition does not affect its validity.

The Principle: Only Omission of Hajj Acts Requires Dam
States and explains the principle that only omission of actual Hajj acts requires dam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that only omission of actual Hajj acts (af'al al-hajj) requires dam, and distinguish between integral Hajj acts and facilitative actions like staying in Mina.

Core Idea
Dam compensates only for omitting a Hajj act, not for leaving a facilitative practice.

The author of Hidayah articulates a critical boundary: not every omission during Hajj triggers compensation. This lesson unpacks that principle and its application to staying in Mina, with a comparison to the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Read the first sentence: 'Whatever is not from the actions of Hajj, its omission does not necessitate the compensator.' Understand that only omission of an actual Hajj act (af'al al-hajj) can require dam.
The Arabic 'الجابر' means 'the compensator', often referring to dam.
2
Define 'Af'al al-Hajj'
Determine what counts as an act of Hajj. In Hanafi fiqh, these include ihram, tawaf, sa'y, wuquf, rami al-jamarat, and other wajib or rukn acts. Acts that are merely facilitative are not considered af'al al-hajj.
Facilitative acts are those ordained to make performance easier, not as integral commands.
3
Apply to Staying in Mina
The passage explains that staying overnight in Mina is not from af'al al-hajj because its purpose is to facilitate rami (stoning). Therefore, intentional omission does not require dam.
The same principle applies to other facilitative acts like staying in Muzdalifah (though some have different rulings).
4
Compare with Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i considers staying in Mina a wajib act, so its omission requires dam. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the purpose (facilitation) and the act itself.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ فَتَرْكُهُ لَا يُوجِبُ الْجَابِرَ . ترجمہ: جو چیز حج کے افعال میں سے نہیں ہے اس کا ترک کرنا نقصان کو ثابت نہیں کرتا۔ تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جو فعل حج کے افعال میں سے نہ ہو اگر اس کو آدمی چھوڑ دے تو اس پر دم وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوتا، کیونکہ دم افعال حج کے کسی فعل کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے آتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی حاجی نے منی کے علاوہ کسی دوسری جگہ جان بوجھ کر رات گزاری تو ہمارے یہاں اس پر دم وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ قیام منی کا ثبوت اس لئے ہے تا کہ حاجی کے لئے رمی کرنا آسان ہو ، لہذا قیام منی افعال حج میں سے نہیں ہو گا اور اس کے ترک پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہوگی جو جبر نقصان کے لئے وضع کی گئی ہے یعنی دم وغیرہ۔ اس کے برخلاف امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کے یہاں چونکہ قیام منی واجب ہے، لہذا اس کے ترک پر دم واجب ہوگا۔ = أَفْضَلُ لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ أَنَّ كُلَّ رَبِّي لَيْسَ بَعْدَهُ رَمَى فَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَرْمِيَهُ رَاكِبًا وَإِلَّا فَمَاشِيًا. تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام ج ۲ ص ۳۰، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الإحرام، ج ۱ ص ۲۷۵، ط: رحمانیہ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَبِيتَ لَيَالِي مِنِّى إِلَّا بِمِنِّى وَكَانَ عُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ يُؤَدِّبُ عَلَى تَرْكِ الْمُقَامِ بِهَا كَذَا فِي الْهِدَايَةِ فَإِنْ بَاتَ فِي غَيْرِهَا مُتَعَمِّدًا لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَيْءٍ عِنْدَنَا لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ لِيَسْهُلَ عَلَيْهِ الرَّمَى فِي أَيَّامِهِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ فَتَرْكُهُ لَا يُوجِبُ الْجَبْرَ.
Whatever is not from the actions of Hajj, its omission does not necessitate the compensator. Translation: The omission of something that is not among the actions of Hajj does not establish deficiency. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that if a person omits an act that is not among the actions of Hajj, then dam etc. are not obligatory upon him, because dam comes due to omitting some action of Hajj. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that if a pilgrim intentionally spends the night in a place other than Mina, then according to us, dam etc. are not obligatory upon him, because the obligation of staying in Mina is to make it easy for the pilgrim to perform the rami (stoning). Therefore, staying in Mina is not among the actions of Hajj, and its omission does not require anything that is prescribed for compensating deficiency, i.e., dam. In contrast, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, since staying in Mina is obligatory, its omission necessitates dam. = It is more virtuous based on what we narrated, and the principle in it is that every pillar after which there is no rami, then it is more virtuous to perform it riding, otherwise walking. (Tabyeen al-Haqa'iq: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Ihram vol.2 p.30, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami) (Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Ihram, vol.1 p.275, Rahmania). It is disliked to spend the nights of Mina except in Mina, and Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to discipline for abandoning staying there. Thus in Al-Hidayah: If he intentionally spends the night elsewhere, nothing is incumbent upon him according to us, because it (staying) was made obligatory to make rami easy for him during its days, so it is not from the actions of Hajj, and its omission does not necessitate compensation.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a key Hanafi principle regarding Hajj: compensation (dam) is only required for omitting actions that are intrinsic to Hajj (af'al al-hajj). The author of Hidayah uses this principle to explain that staying overnight in Mina is not a fundamental Hajj act; it is merely facilitative for prayer and rami. Therefore, intentionally missing it does not require dam according to the Hanafi school. This contrasts with the Shafi'i school, which deems staying in Mina obligatory (wajib). The passage then quotes from Tabyeen al-Haqa'iq and Al-Hidayah to reinforce: it is recommended to perform rami riding if possible, but omitting it does not violate Hajj. Then a longer quote from Hidayah clarifies: Umar ibn al-Khattab used to discipline people for not staying in Mina, yet legally no compensation is due because the ruling is based on facilitation, not an integral Hajj act.

Key Terms
أفعال الحج (af‘al al-hajj): Actions that are part of the Hajj ritual, such as ihram, tawaf, sa‘y, and wuquf.
الجابر (al-jabir): A compensatory act, such as dam (sacrifice), required to make up for an omission in Hajj.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep) offered when a wajib act of Hajj or Umrah is omitted or violated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a pilgrim intentionally spends a night of Mina outside Mina, what is the ruling?
A) Dam is wajib
B) No dam is required
C) The Hajj is invalid
D) A fidyah of fasting is required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts dam to omissions of actual Hajj acts; facilitative acts like staying in Mina do not require compensation.
