A) No penalty because he was asleep
B) Sadaqah only
C) A dam (sheep) is obligatory
D) He must sacrifice an animal and also give charity

Key Takeaway
Sleep and coercion remove sin but not the legal ruling; the cause of benefit triggers dam even without consent.

The Hanafi Definition of Prey and Its Application to Locusts
Defines prey and applies to locusts with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of prey (sayd), apply it to determine whether a locust is prey, and explain the obligation of sadaqah for a muhrim who kills a locust, citing the proof from Umar (RA).

Core Idea
A locust is prey because it requires a stratagem to catch; killing it in ihram demands sadaqah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a key definition: prey (sayd) is any animal that cannot be captured without a stratagem (heelah). This definition determines the ruling for a muhrim who kills a locust. Since a locust cannot be caught easily without a net or trick, it falls under the category of land prey, and its killing in ihram triggers a compensation (sadaqah). The primary proof is the statement of Caliph Umar (RA): 'A date is better than a locust,' which implies that one should give charity for the locust killed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the specific hukm (obligation) for a muhrim who kills a locust?
The act is killing a locust while in ihram. The ruling is that wajib (obligatory) sadaqah must be given.
2
Locate the Dalil
What proof does Al-Marghinani cite for this ruling? Identify the source and type of proof.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (statement of a companion) from Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
How does Umar's statement prove the obligation? What is the legal link between the statement and the ruling?
The statement compares a date (charity) to a locust, implying that a date is more valuable and thus giving charity compensates for the locust.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Do other schools agree that a locust is considered prey? If not, how does this affect the ruling?
Some schools may not classify locusts as sayd, so the ruling differs. This is a mukhtalaf fih issue.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
Which position is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school and why?
The Hanafi position that sadaqah is obligatory is the relied-upon view, supported by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and the authority of Umar's statement.

(213) Indeed, prey is that which cannot be taken except by a stratagem.
Translation: Prey is that whose capture is not possible without a stratagem.
Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that hunting is called that which catching a animal is not possible without a stratagem and device, but for its capture the hunter uses some stratagem like a net etc., and that animal which cannot be caught without a stratagem is not called prey.
The author of Hidayah mentions the mentioned principle and states that if a muhrim kills a locust (جرادة), then he should give some charity as he wishes, because the locust is land prey and its capture is not possible without a stratagem, and that thing whose capture is not possible without a stratagem is prey, and if a muhrim hunts, then upon him is compensation according to the size of that thing, therefore upon him too sadaqah becomes obligatory, due to the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): "A date is better than a locust."
And according to us, due to sleep and coercion, sin is removed without the ruling, meaning the sin which is the ruling of the Hereafter is removed without the ruling that relates to blood; and its cause has been established, i.e., the cause of the obligation of the ransom, and the waw is for the state (and it is) i.e., the cause is what he obtains of relief and adornment, i.e., what the shaved person obtains of adornment and relief by the removal of dishevelment, and from adornment by the removal of scattered hair.
Al-Binayah: Book of Hajj, Chapter of Crimes, vol. 4 p. 338, ed. Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyyah]
Al-Hidayah: Book of Hajj, Chapter of Crimes, section, vol. 1 p. 303, ed. Rahmaniyyah
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage defines 'sayd' (prey) in the Hanafi school as an animal that cannot be captured without a stratagem (heelah). This definition determines the ruling for a muhrim who kills a locust (جرادة). Since the locust is a land animal that requires a net or trick to catch, it qualifies as prey, and the muhrim must pay sadaqah (charity) as compensation. The proof for this ruling includes the statement of Caliph Umar (RA): 'A date is better than a locust' (indicating that a date given in charity is more valuable than killing a locust). The passage also repeats the Arabic text from the previous lesson about sleep and coercion, but that appears to be a scribal duplication; the main focus is on the definition of prey and its application to locusts. The mufta bihi ruling is that killing a locust in ihram requires sadaqah, the amount of which is based on the size of the locust (typically a few dates or similar food).

Key Terms
صید (sayd): Prey; any wild animal that cannot be caught without a stratagem. Includes locusts according to this definition.
حیلہ (heelah): A stratagem, trick, or device used to capture game, such as a net or trap.
جراد (jaraad): Locust; a kind of insect considered part of land prey (sayd al-barr) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No, because it is not a land animal

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any animal that cannot be captured without a stratagem is prey, and killing it in ihram requires compensation, as demonstrated by the locust case with Umar's statement as proof.

Dam for a Sleeping or Coerced Muhrim: Ruling and Cause
States the ruling that dam is obligatory for a sleeping or coerced muhrim whose hair is shaved.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that dam is obligatory for a muhrim whose head is shaved while asleep or coerced, and explain the cause (sabab) behind the obligation.

Core Idea
Dam is wajib even without sin — the cause is the benefit of relief, not intention.

One might think that being asleep or forced absolves a muhrim from any penalty for having his head shaved. But the Hanafi school teaches otherwise. In this lesson, we examine a ruling with proof that illustrates a key principle: compensation can be required based on objective cause, not just subjective intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is having a muhrim's head shaved while he is asleep or coerced. The ruling is that dam (a sacrificial penalty) is obligatory upon him.
The text begins: 'صدقہ ہے اور جس کا حلق کیا ہے اس پر دم لازم ہے' meaning dam is necessary.
2
Note the exception: sin is removed
The text explicitly states that due to sleep or coercion, the sin (ithm) is removed — the person is not sinful in the afterlife. However, the worldly ruling (dam) remains.
The key phrase: 'وعندنا بسبب النوم والإكراه ينتفى المأثم دون الحكم'.
3
Locate the cause (sabab)
The passage identifies the cause for dam as 'ما نال من الراحة والزينة' — the attainment of relief and beautification from removing unkempt hair.
This cause is objective and exists regardless of the muhrim's state.
4
Apply the cause to the cases
Both the sleeping and coerced muhrim attain relief and beautification from the shaving. Therefore, the cause is present, and dam is wajib.
Consent or intent is irrelevant to the cause.
5
Understand the type of proof (istihsan)
The proof is based on istihsan: although the sin is removed by sleep/coercion, the ruling remains because the cause for compensation is established. This is a Hanafi principle prioritising the objective benefit.
This contrasts with schools that tie liability to intent.

Sadaqah is (required) and the one whose head is shaved, dam is obligatory upon him. The reason for this is that shaving without the command of the creation in such a way that he was asleep or was forced to shave causes the sin to be removed. That is, the one shaved will not be sinful in the hereafter, but in worldly terms the ruling will be applied, and dam will be obligatory upon him. Even if this shaving occurred without his permission, still dam is obligatory because the cause for the obligation of dam is the attainment of relief and beautification. And this cause exists in the case of the sleeping and the coerced person. And according to us, due to sleep and coercion, the sin is removed but not the ruling, meaning the sin which is the ruling of the afterlife is removed, but not the ruling that pertains to blood (i.e., dam). And its cause has been established, that is, the cause for the obligation of fidyah. And the waw (in the phrase) is for the state (i.e., the cause is what is attained of relief and beautification, meaning what the shaved person attains of beautification and relief by removing unkemptness, and of beautification by removing scattered hair). Al-Binaya, Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties, vol. 4 p. 338, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a cause (ta'lil) from the Hanafi school. It states that a muhrim who has his head shaved while asleep or under coercion must still pay dam (a sacrificial penalty). The rationale is that the obligation of dam is not based on sinfulness (which is removed by lack of intent) but on the attainment of relief and beautification – resulting from the removal of hair – which is a benefit that occurs regardless of consent. The cause (sabab) is the benefit itself, present in both cases. The Arabic extract from Al-Binaya confirms that the sin (ithm) is waived but the ruling (hukm) pertaining to blood remains because the cause for the fidyah (dam) is established. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that rulings can be tied to objective causes rather than subjective intent, especially in matters of compensation.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial penalty (usually a sheep or goat) required for certain violations during ihram, such as shaving hair or killing game.
مکرہ (mukrah): A person who is coerced or forced to perform an action against their will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because sin is not considered in hajj penalties
B) Because the cause (benefit of relief) exists
C) Because the shaver is liable for the act
D) Because the muhrim must pay for any violation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of dam for a muhrim's hair removal is based on the attainment of relief (intifa' rahat), not on sinful intent.

The Hanafi Definition of Sa'yd and the Ruling on Killing a Locust in Ihram
Defines sa'yd and applies to locust with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sa'yd, identify the evidence from the companion Umar, and apply it to rule that killing a locust in ihram requires sadaqah.

Core Idea
A quarry is anything that cannot be caught without a trick—applied to locusts, killing it in ihram requires sadaqah.

This lesson examines a key principle from Al-Hidayah: the definition of sa'yd (quarry) and its application to the locust. Understanding this definition is crucial for a muhrim who encounters a locust during hajj or umrah, for the Hanafi school rules that killing it requires sadaqah, based on the precedent of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is killing a locust (jaradah) while in the state of ihram. The ruling is that sadaqah (charity) becomes wajib (obligatory) upon the muhrim.
The amount of sadaqah is not fixed; Umar's statement suggests a date as a minimum.
2
Understand the definition of sa'yd
The passage defines sa'yd as 'that which cannot be taken except by a trick (hilah) and the taker intends it.' This definition includes land animals that are not easily caught without some strategy, such as using a net.
The condition 'intends it' distinguishes hunting from accidental killing.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab (رضي الله عنه): 'A date is better than a locust.' This is a companion's ruling (qawl sahabi), which is a legitimate source of proof in the Hanafi school.
Umar's statement is taken as indicating that a penalty applies for killing a locust, with a date as a sufficient sadaqah.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Umar's comparison of a date to a locust implies that the locust is considered sa'yd, because a penalty is prescribed. The phrase 'better than' indicates that giving a date as sadaqah is adequate, thus establishing that killing a locust incurs a penalty.
The Hanafis derive that the penalty is not fixed rigidly but can be determined by ijtihad (taqdir bi al-ijtihad).
5
Apply the ruling
Therefore, any muhrim who kills a locust (or any animal that fits the definition of sa'yd) must give sadaqah. The amount is left to his discretion, but at least a date or its equivalent is recommended.
This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ: شکار وہ ہے کہ اس کا پکڑنا بغیر حیلے کے ممکن نہ ہو۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شکار کرنا اس کو کہیں گے کہ جس جانور کا پکڑنا حیلے اور تدبیر کے بغیر ممکن نہ ہو، بلکہ اس کے پکڑنے کے لئے شکاری کوئی حیلہ کرے جیسے جال وغیرہ، اور جس جانور کو بغیر حیلے کے پکڑ ناممکن ہو اس کو شکار نہیں کہتے ہیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں اگر محرم نے جرادہ یعنی ٹڈی کو قتل کر دیا تو کچھ صدقہ کر دے جو چاہے، کیونکہ ٹڈی خشکی کا شکار ہے اور اس کا پکڑ نا بغیر حیلے کے ممکن نہیں ہے اور جس شئی کا پکڑنا بغیر حیلے کے ممکن نہ ہو وہ شکار ہوتی ہے، اور محرم اگر شکار کرے تو اس پر اس شئی کی جسامت کے لحاظ سے تاوان لازم آتا ہے، لہذا اس پر بھی صدقہ لازم آئے گا، لقول عمر رضی اللہ
عنه تَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ
الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات فصل، ج ۱ ص ۳۰۳، ط: رحمانیه وَأَمَّا وُجُوبُهَا بِقَتْلِ الْجَرَادَةِ فَلَّانَّ الْجَرَادَ مِنْ صَيْدِ الْبَرِّ فَإِنَّ الصَّيْدَ مَا لَا يُمْكِنُ أَخُذُهُ إِلَّا بحِيلَةٍ وَيَقْصِدُهُ الْآخِذُ ، وَقَالَ: عُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ تَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ.
البحر الرائق: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات ، ج ۳ ص ۳۷، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
(213) Indeed, the quarry is that which cannot be taken except by a trick. Translation: Quarry is that the catching of which is not possible without a trick. Commentary: The meaning of this principle is that hunting is called (that) for which catching an animal is not possible without a trick and strategy; rather, for its catching, the hunter employs a trick like a net etc. And the animal that can be caught without a trick is not called quarry. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a muhrim kills a locust, he should give some sadaqah as he wishes, because the locust is land quarry and its catching is not possible without a trick, and any thing whose catching is not possible without a trick is quarry, and if a muhrim hunts, then upon him a penalty (tawan) is due according to the size of the thing, so upon him sadaqah is also obligatory. Due to the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'A date is better than a locust.' Al-Hidayah: Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties, vol. 1 p. 303, Rahmania edition: 'And as for its obligation by killing the locust, because the locust is from the land quarry, for indeed the quarry is that which cannot be taken except by a trick and the taker intends it, and Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: A date is better than a locust.' Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: Book of Hajj, Chapter of Penalties, vol. 3 p. 37, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents a definitional ruling (ta'rif hukmi) for the term 'صيد' (sa'yd) in the context of ihram. The Hanafi school defines sa'yd as an animal that cannot be caught without a trick (hilah) and which the hunter deliberately pursues. This definition is used to include the locust (jaradah) as land quarry, for it cannot be caught without a trick. Therefore, if a muhrim kills a locust, he must give sadaqah (charity) as a penalty, following the precedent of Umar (رضي الله عنه) who said a date is better than a locust (i.e., giving a date as sadaqah suffices). The proof is the statement of Umar, which is considered a companion's ruling (qawl sahabi) and is used as a dalil in the Hanafi school. The hidayah text and the later reference from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq confirm this ruling.

Key Terms
صيد (sa'yd): An animal that is hunted and cannot be caught without a trick or strategy.
جراد (jarad): Locust; considered land quarry in the Hanafi school.

B) It cannot be caught without a trick
C) It must be intentionally hunted
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines sa'yd as any animal that cannot be caught without a trick, and this definition includes the locust, making its killing in ihram subject to sadaqah.

Custom (Urf) Takes Precedence Over Literal Meaning
Argues that custom is stronger than linguistic reality in determining meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle 'al-urf amlak' to resolve disputes between custom and literal meaning in oaths and contracts.

Core Idea
Custom overrides literal meaning in legal interpretation, as in the Hanafi view on oaths involving dogs or birds' heads.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi legal maxim: 'Custom has more right.' It is used to resolve a classical dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the scope of the word 'dog' in oaths. By prioritizing common usage over linguistic technicality, the Hanafi school demonstrates how custom functions as a source of law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that Hanafis hold custom (urf) as a binding source that can restrict the literal meaning of words in oaths and contracts.
Principle: al-urf amlak.
2
Identify the opposing school and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the literal linguistic meaning must govern, so 'dog' includes all canines and beasts of prey.
Opposition based on haqiqah lughawiyyah.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
Al-Marghinani (Hidayah) responds that common custom does not apply 'kalb' to beasts; custom is more preponderant.
Evidence: people's understanding.
4
Determine the practical outcome (thamarah al-khilaf)
If someone swears not to eat dog meat, Hanafis allow wolf meat; Shafi'is would not. Similarly for swearing not to eat a head, a bird's head is excluded in Hanafi view.
Concrete examples.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi due to the weight given to consistent custom.
Zahir al-riwayah supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۱۴) إِنَّ الْعُرُفَ أَمْلَكُ .
ترجمہ: عرف زیادہ حقدار ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جوٹھی متعارف بین الناس ہو اس کو حکم اور فیصل بنانا زیادہ مناسب ہے، یعنی بھی متعارف پر عرف کے مطابق حکم مرتب ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کو جواب دے رہے ہیں، امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کلب" لغت کے اعتبار سے درندوں کو بھی شامل ہے، صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عرف میں کلب کا اطلاق درندوں پر نہیں ہوتا۔ عرف حقیقت لغو یہ سے قوی دلیل ہے، اس لئے اگر کوئی قسم کھائے کہ وہ سر نہیں کھائے گا پھر چڑیا کا سر کھائے تو حانث نہیں ہوگا ، اس لئے کہ عرف میں چڑیا کے سر پر اس کا اطلاق نہیں ہوتا ہے، اگر چہ حقیقت کے اعتبار سے وہ سر ہے۔
الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات فصل ج ۱ ص ۳۰۳، ط: رحمانیه واسم الكلب لا يقع على السبع عرفا، والعرف أملك هذا جواب عن قول الشافعي رَحِمَهُ الله وكذا اسم الكلب يتناول السباع لغة.
فأجاب عنه: بأنه لا يقع في عرف الناس بخلاف ما قال، لأنهم لا يفهمون من إطلاق اسم الكلب المعروف عندهم، والعرف أرجح وأقوى من الحقيقة اللغوية، ولهذا إذا حلف لا يأكل رأسًا فأكل رأس العصفور لا يحنث لعدم العرف فيه وإن كان رأسًا في الحقيقة. [البناية كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات، ج ۱ ص ۳۹۹، ط: دار الكتب العلمية ]
(214) Indeed, custom has more right. Translation: Custom has more right. Commentary: The meaning of this principle is that what is customary among people is more appropriate to be made the basis of ruling and judgment, i.e., a ruling will be applied according to the custom. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to respond to Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). Imam Shafi'i says that the word 'dog' (kalb) includes beasts of prey (siba') according to linguistic reality. The author of Al-Hidayah says that in custom, the word 'dog' is not applied to beasts of prey. Custom is stronger evidence than linguistic reality. Therefore, if someone swears that he will not eat a head (ra's), and then eats the head of a sparrow, he does not break his oath because there is no custom (urf) applying the word 'head' to it, even though it is a head in reality. Al-Hidayah: Book of Hajj, Chapter on Penalties, vol. 1 p. 303: 'And the word dog (ism al-kalb) does not apply to beasts of prey in custom, and custom has more right. This is a response to the saying of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), and likewise the word dog includes beasts of prey linguistically. He (al-Marghinani) responded that it does not apply in the custom of people contrary to what he said, because they do not understand from the use of the word 'dog' what is known among them, and custom is more preponderant and stronger than linguistic reality. For this reason, if someone swears that he will not eat a head and then eats a sparrow's head, he does not break his oath due to the lack of custom in it, even though it is a head in reality.' [Al-Binaya, Book of Hajj, Chapter on Penalties, vol. 1 p. 399, Dar al-Kutub al-Ilmiyya]
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim 'العرف أملك' (custom has more right) and uses it in an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The issue is whether the word 'dog' (kalb) in oaths includes beasts of prey like wolves and lions. Al-Shafi'i argues that linguistically it does, so swearing not to touch a dog would include such animals. The Hanafi response is that in common custom (urf), the word 'dog' is only used for the domestic dog, not for wild beasts. Therefore, the custom prevails over the linguistic reality. This is applied to a case where one swears not to eat a 'head' (ra's) — he does not break his oath by eating a bird's head because custom does not apply the term 'head' to that small head, even though it is a head literally. This shows that in Hanafi jurisprudence, custom (urf) is a valid source that can overrule literal meanings in legal interpretation, particularly in oaths and contracts.

Key Terms
عُرْف (urf): Customary practice or common usage among people that is consistent and does not contradict a clear text.
حقيقة لغوية (haqiqah lughawiyyah): The literal, original meaning of a word as defined in Arabic lexicons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He breaks his oath because the oath is general
D) He must expiate for the oath

Key Takeaway
Custom (urf) is a binding source in Hanafi law that can override literal meanings in interpretation of oaths and contracts.

Muhrim: Initiation Prohibited, Defense Permitted
Clarifies that a muhrim may defend himself against animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited initiation (ta'arud) and permissible defense (daf' al-adha) for a muhrim, and apply the ruling to scenarios of self-defense during ihram.

Core Idea
A muhrim may not hunt, but may defend himself; Shari'ah forbids aggression, not self-protection.

This lesson examines a key principle from the Hanafi fiqh of ihram: the distinction between initiating contact with animals and defending oneself. Many assume that during ihram, one cannot harm any creature under any circumstance. However, the Hanafi school clarifies that necessity permits self-defense even if it leads to the animal's death. Understanding this ruling helps avoid confusion about the scope of prohibitions in Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
Recognize that the passage discusses two types of actions: ta'arud (initiating contact) and daf' al-adha (repelling harm). The first is prohibited, the second is permitted.
Focus on the verb 'mumnoo'' (prohibited) and its exception 'la 'an daf''.
2
Define the key terms
Parse ta'arud as proactive aggression (e.g., hunting, catching) and daf' al-adha as reactive self-defense against an actual attack.
The distinction hinges on intentionality: ta'arud is deliberate initiation, daf' is response to harm.
3
Apply the principle to a scenario
Given a hypothetical situation (e.g., a muhrim being attacked by a wolf), determine whether the permissible line is crossed.
Self-defense is allowed even if the animal dies; no penalty is incurred.
4
Note the rationale
Understand that the ruling is based on necessity (darurah) and the Shari'ah objective of preserving life.
The same principle applies to other forms of harm, e.g., killing a scorpion that threatens.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that defense is mubah and does not require any compensation (dam).
This is a settled point with no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۱۵) إِنَّ الْمُحْرِمَ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنِ التَّعَرُضِ لَا عَنْ دَفْعِ الْأَذَى.
ترجمہ: محرم کو تعرض کرنے سے روکا گیا ہے نہ کہ اذیت دور کرنے سے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ محرم کو حالتِ احرام میں شریعت نے درندوں وغیرہ کے ساتھ چھیڑ چھاڑ کرنے سے منع کیا ہے، یعنی کسی جانور وغیرہ کو نہ پکڑے اور شکار نہ کرے لیکن
اپنے دفاع سے شریعت نے اس کو منع نہیں کیا، اس لئے محرم اپنا دفاع کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر محرم پر کسی درندے نے اچانک
الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات ، فصل، ج ۱ ص ۳۰۴، ط: رحمانیه
(215) Indeed, the muhrim is prohibited from initiating contact, not from repelling harm. Translation: The muhrim is prohibited from initiating contact (ta'arud) not from repelling harm (daf' al-adha). Commentary: The meaning of this principle is that the muhrim, during the state of ihram, is prohibited by the Shari'ah from tampering with beasts etc., i.e., he should not catch any animal or hunt, but the Shari'ah has not prohibited him from his own defense, therefore the muhrim can defend himself. The author of Al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a beast suddenly attacks the muhrim... Al-Hidayah: Book of Hajj, Chapter on Penalties, vol. 1 p. 304, Rahmania edition.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling (hukm) about the scope of prohibitions in ihram. The maxim 'المحرم ممنوع عن التعرض لا عن دفع الأذى' (the muhrim is prohibited from initiation, not from repelling harm) distinguishes between proactive aggression and reactive defense. The Shari'ah forbids a muhrim from intentionally initiating contact with animals (hunting, catching, or harming them), but if an animal attacks him, he is permitted to defend himself even if it results in the animal's death, because that is considered repelling harm (daf' al-adha) rather than ta'arud (initiation). This is based on the principle of necessity (darurah) and the broader Shari'ah objective of preserving life. The passage does not provide explicit proof (dalil) but is presented as a foundational rule understood from the sources.

Key Terms
تعرض (ta'arud): Deliberately initiating contact or confrontation, especially in the context of hunting or harming animals during ihram.
دفع الأذى (daf' al-adha): Repelling harm or warding off injury, such as defending oneself from an attacking animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle stated, what may a muhrim do if a wild animal suddenly attacks him?
A) He must not defend himself because he is in ihram
B) He may defend himself but must pay dam if he kills the animal
C) He may defend himself without incurring any penalty
D) He may only run away but not fight back

Key Takeaway
The muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm (ta'arud) but may defend himself (daf' al-adha) against attacking animals without penalty.

Defending Against Attack in Ihram: No Penalty for Self-Defense
Clarifying that prohibitions on a muhrim concern initiating aggression, not defending against harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim killing an attacking animal in self-defense and distinguish between initiation (ta'arruḍ) and repelling harm (daf' al-adha).

Core Idea
A muhrim is forbidden from initiation, not from repelling harm — self-defense incurs no penalty.

In the state of ihram, a person is subject to many prohibitions, including hunting. But what if a wild animal attacks? Does the muhrim have to let himself be harmed? This lesson clarifies a key principle: the prohibition is on initiating aggression, not on defending oneself. The author of al-Hidayah uses this to derive that a muhrim who kills an attacking animal owes nothing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage describes a muhrim who is attacked by a beast and kills it because repelling is only possible by killing. The ruling is clear: 'nothing is upon him' (فلا شيء عليه).
The act is killing in self-defense; the ruling is that no penalty (dam, fidyah, or invalidation) is incurred.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle stated at the beginning: the muhrim is prevented from ta'arruḍ (initiation) but not from daf' al-adha (repelling harm). This is both the ruling's basis and its explicit justification.
The dalil is the qa'ida itself, which is derived from various texts including the hadith about the five harmful animals (fawasiq).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The principle directly shows that the prohibition's scope excludes defense. Therefore, killing in self-defense is not a violation of ihram, and no penalty arises. The 'illa (effective cause) for the prohibition is initiating aggression, not reacting to harm.
This is a talil (ratio legis) argument: the ruling follows from the purposive interpretation of the prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school holds this position, some other scholars might interpret the general prohibition on hunting as comprehensive, thereby requiring expiation even in self-defense. However, the Hanafi view is mufta bihi (relied upon).
The source indicates cross-madhhab difference (mukhtalaf fih), but the Hanafi position is based on necessity (daf' al-adha).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْمُحْرِمَ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنِ التَّعَرُّضِ لَا عَنْ دَفْعِ الْأَذَى.
ترجمہ: محرم کو تعرض کرنے سے روکا گیا ہے نہ کہ اذیت دور کرنے سے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ محرم کو حالتِ احرام میں شریعت نے درندوں وغیرہ کے ساتھ چھیڑ چھاڑ کرنے سے منع کیا ہے، یعنی کسی جانور وغیرہ کو نہ پکڑے اور شکار نہ کرے لیکن
اپنے دفاع سے شریعت نے اس کو منع نہیں کیا، اس لئے محرم اپنا دفاع کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر محرم پر کسی درندے نے اچانک حملہ کر دیا اور محرم نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس صورت میں محرم پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہے، کیونکہ شریعت نے محرم کو تعرض سے منع کیا ہے نہ کہ دفاع سے، لہذا تعرض تو ممنوعات احرام میں سے ہے لیکن دفاع محظورات احرام میں سے نہیں ہے، لہذا محرم نے بھی چونکہ اپنا دفاع کیا ہے اس لئے اس پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
(وإن صال السبع على محرم ولا يمكنه دفعه إلا بقتله فقتله فلا شيء عليه) لأنه ممنوع عن التعرض لا عن دفع الأذى.
اللباب في شرح الكتاب: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات، ج ۱ ص ۲۱۵، ط: المكتبة العلمية
Indeed, the muhrim is prevented from initiation, not from repelling harm. Translation: The muhrim is prohibited from initiating aggression, not from repelling harm. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that in the state of ihram, the Shari'ah has prohibited the muhrim from messing with beasts etc., i.e., he should not catch any animal nor hunt. However, the Shari'ah has not prohibited him from defending himself. Therefore, the muhrim can defend himself. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a beast suddenly attacks a muhrim and the muhrim kills it, then nothing is incumbent upon him in that case, because the Shari'ah has prohibited him from initiation, not from defense. Thus, initiation is among the prohibitions of ihram, but defense is not among the forbidden acts of ihram. Hence, since the muhrim defended himself, nothing is incumbent upon him. (And if a beast attacks a muhrim and he cannot repel it except by killing it, and he kills it, then nothing is upon him) because he is prevented from initiation, not from repelling harm.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage explains a key distinction in the prohibitions of ihram. A muhrim is forbidden from initiating any action that would involve hunting or harming animals (ta'arruḍ). However, if an animal attacks the muhrim and he kills it in self-defense, there is no penalty (shay' 'alayh) because the prohibition is on initiation, not on repelling harm. This is consistent with the broader Shari'ah principle that necessity permits otherwise prohibited acts. The ruling is supported by the hadith about the five harmful animals that may be killed in ihram (fawasiq), which is a permission for potential harm. By way of priority (awla), when harm is actualized, the permission is even stronger.

Key Terms
التعرض (al-ta'arruḍ): Initiation of aggression or interference with an animal
دفع الأذى (daf' al-adha): Repelling harm that is actually or potentially coming towards the muhrim
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must pay penalty (dam).
B) He must make up for it with fidyah.
C) Nothing is incumbent upon him.
D) His ihram becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may defend himself against attack without incurring penalty — the prohibition covers initiation, not defense.

The Principle of Permission Negating Compensation
Stating a principle with talil reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that permission from the Lawgiver eliminates compensation and apply it to cases of killing harmful animals during ihram.

Core Idea
When the Lawgiver permits an act, no penalty applies – permission eliminates liability.

This lesson unpacks a foundational maxim from the Hidayah: permission from the Shari' removes liability for compensation. We will see how this principle applies to a muhrim who kills harmful animals, even when the harm is only anticipated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Recognize the maxim 'Indeed, compensation is not obligatory with the existence of permission from the Lawgiver'. Understand that when the Shari'ah explicitly permits an action, no penalty (jaza') is due.
2
Understand the Context: Ihram and Harmful Animals
The specific case is a muhrim killing animals that cause harm. The Shari'ah permits killing the five 'fawasiq' (snake, scorpion, mouse, biting dog, crow) even when harm is only anticipated (mutawahham).
The list of fawasiq may vary; the Hanafi school includes these five.
3
Apply the Principle of Awla (Priority)
If anticipated harm permits killing, then certain harm (mutahaqqaq) permits it by even stronger reasoning (awla). The text uses 'awla' to extend the permission.
4
Conclude: No Liability
Since the Lawgiver granted permission (either explicitly for fawasiq or by awla for certain harm), no penalty (jaza') is wajib on the muhrim.
This applies to self-defense or repelling unavoidable harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْجَزَاءَ لَا يَجِبُ مَعَ وُجُوْدِ الْإِذْنِ مِنَ الشَّارِعِ.
ترجمہ: شارع کی طرف سے اجازت کے پائے جانے کے ساتھ بدلہ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب شارع کی جانب سے کسی ممنوع فعل کی اجازت ہو تو اس فعل کے ارتکاب سے کچھ بدلہ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ محرم آدمی کو اس اذیت کو دفع کرنے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے جو متوہم ہو ، یعنی جن سے تکلیف پہنچنے کا وہم ہو، جیسے فواسق جانور (سانپ، بچھو، چوہا، کاٹنے والا کتا) وغیرہ۔ تو جس چیز کا تکلیف دینا متحقق ہو، یعنی یقین ہو کہ یہ اذیت پہنچائے گی تو اس کو دفع کرنے کی تو بطریق اولی اجازت ہوگی ، اور شارع کی طرف سے اجازت کے ساتھ کچھ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا محرم شخص اگر اپنے سے اذیت دور کرنے کے لئے حملہ آور درندے کو قتل کر دیتا ہے تو اس پر ضمان وغیرہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ جب شریعت نے فواسق خمسہ میں اذیت کے وہم کی وجہ سے انہیں مارنے کی اجازت دی ہے تو پھر وہ جانور جن میں اذیت متحقق ہے انہیں تو بدرجہ اولی مارنے کی اجازت ہوگی ۔
ثم قال: هُوَ مَأْذُونٌ لَهُ فِي قَتْلِ الْمُتَوَهَّمِ مِنْهُ الْأَذَى كَمَا فِي الْفَوَاسِقِ فَلَانُ يَكُونَ مَأْذُونَا فِي دَفْعِ الْمُتَحَقِّقِ أَوْلَى وَمَعَ وُجُودِ الْإِذْنِ مِنْ الشَّارِعِ لَا يَجِبُ الْجَزَاءُ حَقًّا.
Indeed, compensation is not obligatory with the existence of permission from the Lawgiver. Translation: When permission from the Lawgiver is present, compensation is not obligatory. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when there is permission from the Lawgiver for a prohibited act, then committing that act does not incur any compensation. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that a muhrim is permitted to repel harm that is anticipated (mutawahham), i.e., from which harm is expected, like the five harmful animals (snake, scorpion, mouse, biting dog, etc.). Then that which harm is certain (mutahaqqaq) to cause harm, it is by greater reason permitted to repel it, and with the existence of permission from the Lawgiver, compensation is not obligatory. Therefore, if a muhrim kills an attacking beast to repel harm from himself, he is not liable for compensation (daman), etc. When the Shari'ah allowed killing the five harmful animals due to anticipated harm, then those animals from which harm is certain are even more clearly allowed to be killed. Then he said: He is permitted to kill that from which harm is anticipated, as in the case of the fawasiq, so he would be permitted to repel that which harm is certain even more clearly, and with the existence of permission from the Lawgiver, compensation is not obligatory as a right.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This principle builds on the previous one by providing a rationale: when the Lawgiver (al-Shari') grants permission for an action, no penalty (jaza') applies. The specific context is killing harmful animals in ihram. The Shari'ah explicitly permits killing the 'five harmful animals' (fawasiq) even when the harm is only anticipated (mutawahham). By priority of reasoning (awla), if harm is certain (mutahaqqaq), the permission is even stronger. Therefore, a muhrim who kills an animal in self-defense incurs no liability, because the action is permissible and permission negates compensation.

Key Terms
الجزاء (al-jaza'): Compensation, penalty, or expiation for forbidden acts, such as dam or fidyah
الإذن من الشارع (al-idhn min al-shari'): Permission from the Lawgiver (Allah and His Messenger) to perform an act
المتوهم منه الأذى (al-mutawahham minhu al-adha): That from which harm is anticipated, like the five fawasiq

No Compensation with Permission from the Lawgiver
Stating and explaining the principle that permission negates liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that Shari‘ah permission negates liability and apply it to the scenario of a muhrim defending against an attacking animal.

Core Idea
Permission from the Lawgiver removes liability for defensive acts during ihram.

In this lesson, we explore a key legal principle from the Hanafi school: when the Lawgiver explicitly or implicitly permits an act, no compensation (jaza') is due even if that act would normally be prohibited. This principle is particularly relevant for a muhrim (someone in the state of ihram) who is attacked and must defend themselves. The passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that defense is not aggression, and since the Shari‘ah permits repelling harm, the muhrim incurs no penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
Consider the scenario: a muhrim is attacked by a beast (e.g., a tiger or wolf) and kills it in self-defense. Note that the muhrim is in a state where hunting and killing animals are generally prohibited.
The beast is not among the fawasiq (harmful animals) but is a threat.
2
State the legal principle
The passage quotes the principle: 'Compensation is not obligatory when there is permission from the Lawgiver.' Understand that this is a general qa'idah applicable beyond this case.
The principle is expressed in Arabic as: إن الجزاء لا يجب مع وجود الإذن من الشارع
3
Distinguish aggression from defense
The key is that the muhrim is prohibited from initiating aggression (ta'arruḍ) but not from repelling harm (daf' al-adha). Permission covers defensive acts only.
Aggression would still incur liability.
4
Apply the principle via a fortiori reasoning
The Shari‘ah already permits killing the five fawasiq (snake, scorpion, etc.) even when harm is merely anticipated. When harm is certain, as in a direct attack, the permission is even stronger.
This is an argument from the lesser to the greater (awlā).
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the muhrim who kills the attacking beast owes no compensation (jaza') and no guarantee (daman). The act is permissible and liability-free.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text

(وإن صال السبع على محرم ولا يمكنه دفعه إلا بقتله فقتله فلا شيء عليه) لأنه ممنوع عن التعرض لا عن دفع الأذى.

الجوهرة النيرة : كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات، ج ا ص ٦ ١ ، ط: المطبعة الخيرية
If a beast attacks a muhrim and he cannot repel it except by killing it, so he kills it, then nothing is due from him. Because he is prohibited from aggression, not from repelling harm. Principle (216): Indeed, compensation is not obligatory when there is permission from the Lawgiver. Translation: With the presence of permission from the Lawgiver, recompense is not obligatory. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when the Lawgiver permits a prohibited act, then no recompense is obligatory for committing that act. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to state that a muhrim is permitted to repel harm that is anticipated, i.e., from which harm is feared, like the five harmful animals (snake, scorpion, mouse, biting dog) etc. So for something whose causing of harm is certain, i.e., it is known that it will cause harm, repelling it is permitted a fortiori, and with permission from the Lawgiver nothing is obligatory. Therefore, if a muhrim kills an attacking beast to repel harm from himself, compensation etc. is not obligatory upon him. Since the Shari'ah permitted killing the five harmful animals due to anticipated harm, then for animals where harm is certain, they are permitted to be killed a fortiori.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents a legal principle (qā‘idah) from the Hanafi school regarding the actions of a muhrim (a person in the state of ihrām for Hajj or ‘Umrah). The passage type is a ruling with explanation. The author begins by describing a scenario: a beast attacks a muhrim, and he can only defend himself by killing it. The ruling is that nothing is due from the muhrim—no compensation, no sin. The reason is that the Shari‘ah prohibits a muhrim from initiating aggression (ta‘arruḍ) but not from self-defense (difā‘). The principle is then stated: 'Compensation is not obligatory when there is permission from the Lawgiver.' This principle is applied: the Shari‘ah permits a muhrim to kill the five harmful animals (the fawāsiq) even if only harm is anticipated. Therefore, when harm is certain, it is even more permitted to repel it. The commentary explains that the allowance is for defense, not aggression. The passage then quotes from al-Lubāb, al-Hidāyah, and al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah to show that this is the established Hanafi position. The key takeaway is that permission from the Lawgiver negates liability, so a muhrim who kills an attacker is not liable.

Key Terms
جَزَاء (jazā’): Compensation or penalty due for violating prohibitions of ihram, such as killing game. It can be fasting, feeding, or sacrifice.
الْإِذْن مِنَ الشَّارِعِ (al-idhn min al-shāri‘): Permission from the Lawgiver (Allah or His Messenger) explicitly or implicitly allowing an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does a muhrim not owe compensation for killing an attacking beast?
A) Because any killing during ihram is forgiven.
B) Because the muhrim acted in self-defense, which is permitted by the Shari‘ah, and permission negates liability.
C) Because the beast is considered one of the fawasiq.
D) Because the muhrim can claim ignorance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that permission from the Lawgiver negates liability is applied to a muhrim's defensive killing, so no compensation is due.

The Principle of Original Creation: Al-‘Āriḍ Lā Yu‘tabar
Explaining a legal principle through a concrete fiqh example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that accidental attributes do not affect rulings, and explain why a domesticated pigeon is considered wild for purposes of hunting compensation.

Core Idea
Accidental changes never override the original legal nature of a thing.

Islamic law often looks to the essential nature of things rather than temporary states. This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi principle: accidental attributes are irrelevant for rulings. We will see this through the specific case of a domesticated pigeon, which remains legally wild because its original creation (aṣl al-khilqah) is wild.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Locate the core statement: 'Indeed, the accidental (attribute) is not considered.' Understand that it means rulings are based on the original inherent nature, not on temporary or acquired changes.
2
Examine the Application
The author applies the principle to a domesticated pigeon. Note that pigeons are originally wild. Domestication is an accidental attribute, so it does not change the ruling. Thus, a muhrim who kills such a pigeon must pay compensation (jaza').
This is compared to animals like camels that become wild – they lose the ruling of game because their original nature is domestic.
3
Understand the Scope
Recognize that this principle is not limited to pigeons. It applies to any situation where an accidental change could affect a ruling. The key is to determine what is 'original' (aṣl) and what is 'accidental' ('āriḍ).
The text also mentions domesticated gazelles, ostriches, and emus as parallels.
4
Connect to Shari'ah Reasoning
This principle aligns with istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity), but here it is applied to physical nature. Understand that the Hanafi school gives weight to the original creation over later transformations.
The source cites al-Hidayah and Bada’i‘ al-Ṣanā’i‘ as authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۱۷) إِنَّ الْعَارِضَ لَا يُعْتَبَرُ .
ترجمہ: عارض کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جوشی کسی کو عارض ہو یعنی اس کی ذاتی اور خلقتی نہ ہو تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ، یعنی حکم عارض پر مرتب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصل خلقت پر ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ محرم آدمی نے اگر ایسا کبوتر ذبح کیا جو مانوس ہو، یعنی اپنے ساتھ عادی بنایا ہو تو اس پر جزاء ہوگی، کیونکہ کبوتر اصل خلقت کے اعتبار سے وحشی ہے اور اس کا مانوس ہونا عارض ہے، اصلی نہیں ہے۔ احکام شرعیہ میں اصل کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عوارض کا۔ اس لئے یہ وحشی شمار ہو گا اور چونکہ وحشی جانور کو ذبح کرنے کی وجہ سے جزاء لازم ہوتی ہے، لہذا اس محرم پر بھی جزا ءلا زم ہوگی ۔
الهداية: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات، فصل، ج ۱ ص ۳۰۴، ط: رحمانیه
أَنَّ جِئْسَ الْحَمَامِ مُتَوَحْشَ فِي أَصْلِ الْخِلْقَةِ، وَإِنَّمَا يُسْتَأْنَسُ الْبَعْضُ مِنْهُ بِالنَّوَلدِ وَالنَّأْنِيسِ مَعَ بَقَائِهِ صَيْدًا كَالظَّبْيَةِ الْمُسْتَأْنَسَةِ، وَالنَّعَامَةِ الْمُسْتَأْنَسَةِ وَالطُّوطِيُّ وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ حَتَّى يَجِبَ فِيهِ الْجَرَاء. وَكَذَا الْمُسْتَأْنَسُ فِى الْخِلْقَةِ قَدْ يَصِيرُ مُسْتَوْحِشًا كَالْإِبِلِ ، إِذَا تَوَحْشَتُ وَلَيْسَ لَهُ حُكْمُ الصَّيْدِ حَتَّى لَا يَجِبُ فِيهِ الْجَزَاءِ، فَعَلِمَ أَنَّ الْعِبْرَةَ بِالنَّوَحْشِ، وَالِاسْتِثْنَاسِ فِي أَصْلِ الْخِلْقَةِ. بدائع الصنائع: كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات، فصل، ج ۲ ص ۱۹۶، ط: دار الكتب العلمية
(217) Indeed, the accidental (attribute) is not considered. Translation: The accidental is not taken into account. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that whatever is accidental to something, i.e., not inherent and natural, is not considered; i.e., the ruling is not based on the accidental but on the original creation. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to state that if a muhrim slaughters a pigeon that is domesticated, i.e., he has habituated it, then compensation (jaza’) is due upon him, because the pigeon is wild in its original creation, and its domestication is accidental, not original. In Shari‘ah rulings, the original is considered, not the accidents. Therefore, it will be considered wild, and since killing a wild animal necessitates compensation, so compensation is due upon this muhrim. Al-Hidayah: ... The genus of pigeons is wild in its original creation; only some of them become domesticated through breeding and habituation while remaining game, like a domesticated gazelle, an ostrich, an emu, and the like, such that compensation is due for them. Similarly, something domesticated in creation may become wild, like camels when they become wild, and it does not have the ruling of game such that compensation is not due for it. So it is known that consideration is given to wildness, and domestication in the original creation. Bada’i‘ al-Sana’i‘: ...
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents another qā‘idah: 'Accidental attributes are not considered.' The passage type is a ruling explanation. It clarifies that in Islamic law, the inherent nature of a thing is the basis for rulings, not temporary or acquired states. The application given is about a domesticated pigeon. Pigeons are originally wild game (ṣayd). Domestication (istīnās) is an accidental change that does not remove its original status as game. Therefore, if a muhrim kills a domesticated pigeon, compensation (jaza’) is due, just as for wild game. The passage contrasts this with animals like camels that become wild—they lose the ruling of game because their original creation is domestic. The key point: the 'original creation' (aṣl al-khilqah) determines the ruling. The commentary cites al-Hidāyah and Bada’i‘ al-Ṣanā’i‘ to support this principle. The principle teaches that judges should look past superficial changes and consider the essential nature.

Key Terms
عارِض (‘āriḍ): An accidental or non-essential attribute that is not part of the original creation of a thing.
أصل الخلقة (aṣl al-khilqah): The original inherent nature or state of creation of a thing, which determines its legal status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle 'al-‘āriḍ lā yu‘tabar', which of the following determines the ruling for a muhrim killing an animal?
A) The animal's current behavior (wild or tame)
B) The animal's original creation (wild or domestic)
C) The method of killing
D) The muhrim's intention

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the original inherent nature of a thing governs its legal rulings; accidental changes do not override that nature.

Fasting Suitable for Actions Not for Property Damages
Stating a principle limiting fasting to action-based expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between compensation for actions (jaza’ al-af‘al) and liability for property damages (daman al-mahal) and apply the Hanafi rule that fasting suffices only for the former.

Core Idea
Fasting compensates prohibited actions, not property damage; only monetary value suffices for the latter.

This lesson introduces a key principle in Hajj penalties: not all expiations can be fulfilled by fasting. The Hanafi school distinguishes between compensation for actions (like shaving or wearing sewn clothes) and liability for property damage (like killing game in the Haram). While fasting can substitute for the former, it cannot replace monetary payment for the latter. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying the rules of Hajj violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle and its parts
Read the Arabic principle: 'Indeed, fasting is suitable as compensation for actions, not for damages of the object.' Separate it into two halves: what fasting CAN compensate (actions) and what it CANNOT (property damages).
The term 'ḍamān al-mahāl' refers to liability for property damage.
2
Understand the distinction between 'action' and 'property'
In Hanafi jurisprudence, 'actions' include prohibited acts like shaving hair or wearing sewn clothes while in ihram. 'Property' includes objects like game animals or trees in the Haram. The principle dictates different expiation methods.
This distinction is foundational for many Hajj penalty rulings.
3
Apply the principle to a concrete scenario
Consider a non-muhrim person who kills a deer in the Haram. According to the principle, this is property damage. Therefore, fasting is not acceptable; the person must pay the market value of the deer.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may allow fasting for property damages, but the Hanafi school requires monetary payment. This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۱۸) إِنَّ الصَّومَ يُصْلِحُ جَزَاءَ الْأَفْعَالِ لَا ضَمَانَ الْمَحَالَ .
ترجمہ: روزہ افعال کی جزاء تو بن سکتا ہے لیکن محل کا ضمان نہیں بن سکتا۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ممنوع فعل کے ارتکاب کی وجہ سے جو بدلہ لازم ہوتا ہے روزہ اُس کی جزاء بننے کی صلاحیت تو رکھتا ہے، لیکن محل پر جو جنایت واقع ہوتی ہے اس کا بدلہ نہیں بن سکتا، بلکہ حمل کے ضمان پر قیمت لازم ہوگی۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر حلال آدمی نے حرم کے شکار میں سے کسی جانور کو ذبح کر دیا تو اس پر اس شکار کی قیمت دینا واجب ہے، یعنی اس کی قیمت کو فقراء
(218) Indeed, fasting is suitable as compensation for actions, not for damages of the object. Translation: Fasting can be a compensation for actions, but cannot be a liability for the object. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that fasting has the capacity to serve as compensation for the recompense obligated due to committing a prohibited action, but it cannot be a substitute for the damage inflicted upon the object; rather, for damages to the object, the value is obligatory. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to state that if a non-muhrim (ḥillī) person slaughters an animal from the game of the Ḥaram, then it is obligatory upon him to pay the value of that game, i.e., its value to the poor...
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage introduces a third principle: 'Fasting is suitable as compensation for actions, not for damages to the object.' The passage type is a ruling explanation but is incomplete. The principle distinguishes between two types of liability in Ḥajj penalties: compensation for prohibited actions (like shaving hair or wearing sewn clothes) can be fulfilled by fasting, but compensation for damaging property (like killing game or cutting trees) must be paid in value (price). The application: if a non-muhrim kills an animal in the Ḥaram, he must pay its value; fasting is not acceptable. The explanation seems to have a typo ('حمل' probably 'محل'), but the intended meaning is clear. The passage ends abruptly, but the core idea is that fasting cannot substitute for property damages; only monetary payment works. The passage is from the chapter on penalties in Ḥajj.

Key Terms
ضمان المحال (ḍamān al-mahāl): Liability for damages to an object or property, distinct from compensation for actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because fasting is valid for any sin.
B) No, because fasting is only for compensation of actions, not for property damages.
C) Yes, but only if the person is poor.
D) No, and the person must instead perform a pilgrimage.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: fasting compensates prohibited actions but not property damage; for property, monetary value is required.

Widespread Custom as a Proof in Shari'ah
Explanation of the legal maxim that widespread custom is a valid proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that widespread custom is a valid proof (hujja) and apply it to the case of a muhrim possessing game.

Core Idea
Widespread custom can be a valid proof in Hanafi fiqh, as shown by the Companions' practice of not releasing game while in ihram.

This lesson explores a fundamental Hanafi principle: widespread custom (al-‘ādah al-fāshiyah) is one of the proofs (hujaj). The text from Al-Hidayah uses the example of a person in ihram who already owns game—must he release it? By examining the custom of the Companions, the Hanafi school derives the ruling that no release is required. This demonstrates how custom operates as a subsidiary source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
Recognize that the text introduces the principle that widespread custom is one of the proofs (min ihdā al-ḥujaj). This maxim is being used as evidence for a specific ruling.
2
Understand the Case
The specific issue is whether a muhrim must release game already in his possession (e.g., in his house or cage) upon entering ihram.
3
Examine the Dalil
The proof cited is the widespread custom of the Companions: they would enter ihram while having game in their houses and did not release it, and this practice was well-known and continuous.
The text quotes: 'لأَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كَانُوا يُحْرِمُونَ ، وَفِي بُيُوتِهِمْ صُيُودٌ وَدَوَاجِنُ، وَلَمْ يُنْقَلُ عَنْهُمْ إِرْسَالُهَا'
4
Apply the Maxim
Since widespread custom is a valid proof, this continuous practice establishes that it is not obligatory to release the game. The obligation is only to avoid disturbing the game, which is not happening here because it is confined.
5
Distinguish the Prohibitions
The text also distinguishes between the prohibition due to ihram (which incurs a penalty for the action of hunting) and the prohibition of the sanctuary itself (which imposes a guarantee on the game). Here, the game is owned before ihram and not disturbed, so no penalty applies.
Arabic: 'إِنَّ الْحُرُمَةَ فِي الْمُحْرِمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَعْنَى فِيهِ، وَهُوَ إِحْرَامُهُ فَيَكُونُ جَزَاء الْفِعْلِ، وَهُوَ الْكَفَّارَةُ'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۱۹) إِنَّ الْعَادَةَ الْفَاشِيَةَ مِنْ إِحْدَى الْحُجَجِ . ترجمہ: وہ عادت جو شائع اور مشہور ہو دلائل میں سے ایک دلیل ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس چیز پر عادت جاری ہو اور وہ عادت شائع اور مشہور بھی ہو تو دلائل میں سے ایک دلیل ہے، لہذا اس سے استدلال کرنا درست ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کرے اس بات کو ثابت کر رہے ہیں کہ جس آدمی نے احرام باندھا اس حال میں کہ اس کے گھر یا پنجرے میں اس کے پاس شکار تھا تو اس شخص پر اس شکار کو چھوڑنا اور آزاد کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے، کیونکہ صحابہ کرام احرام باندھے تھے اور ان کے گھروں میں شکار ہوتے تھے لیکن کسی سے یہ منقول نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس شکار کو آزاد کر کے حج پر جاتے ہوں، لہذا اس پر عادت مستمرہ جاری ہے اور عادت چونکہ دلائل میں سے ایک دلیل ہے، لہذا اس شخص پر بھی شکار کو چھوڑ نا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ محرم نے اس کی طرف حالتِ احرام میں تعرض نہیں کیا، إِنَّ الْحُرُمَةَ فِي الْمُحْرِمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَعْنَى فِيهِ، وَهُوَ إِحْرَامُهُ فَيَكُونُ جَزَاء الْفِعْلِ، وَهُوَ الْكَفَّارَةُ وَالْحُرُمَةُ فِي صَيْدِ الْحَرَمِ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَعْنًى فِى الصَّيْدِ فَصَارَ بَدَلَ الْمَحَلَّ وَالصَّوْمِ يَصْلُحُ جَزَاء الْأَفْعَالِ لَا ضَمَانَ الْمَحَلِّ. تبيين الحقائق كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات، فصل، ج ۲ ص ۲۸، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] بلکہ وہ شکار حالت احرام سے پہلے ہی اس کی ملکیت میں تھے۔ ممانعت حالت احرام میں شکار کی طرف تعرض ہے نہ کہ پہلے سے ملکیت کا ہونا۔ لأَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ كَانُوا يُحْرِمُونَ ، وَفِي بُيُوتِهِمْ صُيُودٌ وَدَوَاجِنُ، وَلَمْ يُنْقَلُ عَنْهُمْ إِرْسَالُهَا وَبِذَلِكَ جَرَتِ الْعَادَةُ الْفَاشِيَةُ، وَهِيَ مِنْ إحْدَى الْحُجَجِ ، وَلَانَّ الْوَاجِبَ عَدَمُ التَّعَرُّضِ، وَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِمُتَعَرِّضِ مِنْ جِهَتِهِ لأنَّهُ مَحْفُوظٌ بِالْبَيْتِ وَالْقَفَص لَا بِهِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ فِي مِلْكِهِ. [البحر الرائق: كتاب الحج، باب الجنایات ، فصل، ج ۳ ص ۴۵، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الجنايات فصل ج ۱ ص ۳۰۸، ط: رحمانیه
Translation: That custom which is widespread and well-known is one of the proofs. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that a thing upon which custom is established and that custom is also widespread and well-known, then it is one of the proofs, therefore it is correct to use it as evidence. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is proving that a person who entered ihram while having game in his house or cage, then it is not necessary for him to release and free that game, because the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) would enter ihram while there were game and domestic birds in their houses, and it has not been transmitted from them that they would release them, and upon this the widespread custom has continued, and since custom is one of the proofs, therefore it is not necessary for that person to release the game. Because the Muhrim did not disturb it while in the state of ihram, 'Indeed the prohibition (hurma) in the Muhrim is due to a meaning in him, which is his ihram, so it becomes the penalty of the action, which is the kaffarah, and the prohibition in the hunting of the sanctuary is due to a meaning in the hunting, so it became a substitute for the place, and fasting is suitable as a penalty for actions, not as a guarantee (daman) of the place.' [Tabyin al-Haqaiq: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Jinayat, Fasl, vol 2 p 28, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami] Rather, the game was in his ownership before the state of ihram. The prohibition is in disturbing the game during ihram, not in having ownership beforehand. Because the Companions would enter ihram, and in their houses there were game and domestic birds, and it has not been transmitted from them that they released them, and upon that the widespread custom continued, and it is one of the proofs. And because the obligation is not to disturb, and he is not disturbing from his side because it is confined by the house and cage, not by him, but it is in his ownership. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Jinayat, Fasl, vol 3 p 45, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami] Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Jinayat, Fasl, vol 1 p 308, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage expounds the legal maxim 'Widespread custom is one of the proofs' (العادة الفاشية من إحدى الحجج). The author uses the example of a person who enters ihram while having game in his possession. The question is whether he must release it. By relying on the widespread custom of the Companions who did not release their game when in ihram, the Hanafi school concludes that it is not obligatory. The text also cites an Arabic passage distinguishing between the prohibition due to ihram (which makes the person liable for penalties) and the prohibition of the sanctuary itself (which imposes a guarantee on the game). The key point is that the custom of the Companions serves as a valid proof (hujja) in establishing the ruling.

Key Terms
العادة الفاشية (al-‘ādah al-fāshiyah): The custom that is widespread and well-known, considered one of the proofs (hujaj) in the Hanafi school for deriving rulings when there is no explicit text.
الحجج (al-ḥujaj): Proofs or evidences in Shari'ah. Here it refers to the sources of law, including custom.
محرِم (muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, during which certain prohibitions apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence for the ruling that a person in ihram does not have to release game already in his possession?
A) The Quran
B) The widespread custom of the Companions
C) Qiyas
D) Istihsan

Key Takeaway
Widespread custom (al-‘ādah al-fāshiyah) is a valid proof in Hanafi law, as demonstrated by the Companions' practice of not releasing game while in ihram.

The Arrival of the Substitute is Like the Arrival of the Original
Explains a Hanafi maxim with a scenario from ḥajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'wuṣūl al-khalaf ka-wuṣūl al-aṣl' and apply it to determine liability for compensation in cases involving game removed from the sanctuary.

Core Idea
Paying the substitute (compensation) fulfills the obligation just as returning the original does.

This lesson introduces a foundational Hanafi maxim that equates the arrival of a substitute with the arrival of the original. The maxim is applied to a specific case in ḥajj: a person removes a female gazelle from the sacred sanctuary (ḥaram). If the gazelle later gives birth and both die, the person owes compensation. However, if compensation is paid before the birth, the offspring are not subject to compensation. Understanding this maxim clarifies the legal effect of fulfilling obligations through substitutes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim
Locate the Arabic phrase 'إِنَّ وُصُولَ الْخَلْفِ كَوُصُول الأصل' and understand its literal meaning: 'The arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original.'
This is a general principle, not limited to ḥajj.
2
Analyze the Application Case
Consider the scenario: a person removes a female gazelle from the sanctuary. After removal, she gives birth, then both die. The author rules that the person is liable for compensation for both.
The liability arises because the game still enjoys legal protection (amn) even after removal.
3
Apply the Maxim to the Ruling
If the person pays the compensation for the mother before she gives birth, then the mother is no longer legally protected. When she later gives birth and dies, no compensation is required for the offspring.
The payment of compensation (substitute) is treated exactly like returning the original to the sanctuary.
4
Generalize the Principle
The maxim applies wherever a substitute (like compensation, price, or replacement) fulfills the same obligation as the original object.
In Hanafi fiqh, this supports the idea that performance of an obligation through its substitute is fully valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲۰) إِنَّ وُصُولَ الْخَلْفِ كَوُصُول الأصل. ترجمہ : بدل کا پہنچ جانا اصل کے پہنچنے کی مانند ہے۔ تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نائب کا پہنچ جانا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ اصل پہنچ گیا ، اور جو حکم اصل کے پہنچنے کی صورت میں مرتب ہو گا وہی حکم بدل کے پہنچنے کی صورت میں بھی دائر ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے ہرن کو حرم سے باہر نکالا ، پھر اس ہرن نے بچے جنے اور ہرن بھی مر گئی اور اس کے بچے بھی مر گئے تو اس نکالنے والے پر ان کی جزاء واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ ہرن حرم سے نکالے جانے کے بعد بھی شرعا مستحق امن ہے،اسی وجہ سے اس کو اس کی جاہ امن میں لے جانا واجب ہے، ہاں اگر اس نکالنے والے نے ہرن کی جزاء ادا کر دی پھر اس نے جنا تو اس پر بچوں کی جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ جزاء ادا کرنے کے بعد و مستحق امن نہ رہی، کیونکہ بدل یعنی قیمت کا فقراء کی طرف پہنچ جانا ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ ہرن کا حرم میں پہنچ جانا، اس لئے کہ اصول ہے کہ وصول بدل وصول اصل کی مانند ہوتا ہے۔ أَخْرَجَ ظَبْيَةَ الْحَرَمِ فَوَلَدَتْ فَمَاتَا ضَمِنَهُمَا فَإِنْ أَدَّى جَزَاء هَا فَوَلَدَتْ لَا يَضْمَنُ الْوَلَدَ) لأنَّ الصَّيْدَ بَعْدَ الْإِخْرَاجِ مِنْ الْحَرَمِ بَقِيَ مُسْتَحَقَّ الْأَمْنِ شَرُعًا وَلِهَذَا وَجَبَ رَدُّهُ إِلَى مَأْمَنِهِ، وَهَذِهِ صِفَةٌ شَرْعِيَّةٌ فَتَسْرِى إِلَى الْوَلَدِ فَإِنْ أَدَّى جَزَاء هَا ثُمَّ وَلَدَتْ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ جَزَاءُ الْوَلَدِ، لِأَنَّ بَعْدَ أَدَاءِ الْجَزَاءِ لَمْ تَبْقَ آمِنَةً، لَّانَّ وُصُولَ الْخَلْفِ كَوُصُولِ الْأَصْلِ. البحر الرائق: كتاب الحج، باب إضافة الإحرام ، ج ۱ ص ۳۰۴، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
The arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original. Translation: The arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the arrival of the deputy is like the arrival of the original, and the ruling that would apply in the case of the arrival of the original will also apply in the case of the arrival of the substitute. The author of Hidayah, by mentioning this principle, is explaining that if a person took a female gazelle out of the sanctuary, then she gave birth and both died, then he is liable for them (the compensation). If he paid her compensation and then she gave birth, he is not liable for the offspring. Because the game after being taken out of the sanctuary still deserved protection (amn) legally, and therefore it is obligatory to return it to its place of safety. This is a legal description, so it extends to the offspring. If he paid her compensation and then she gave birth, he is not liable for the offspring, because after paying the compensation she is no longer protected. Because the arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab Ida' al-Ihram, vol 1 p 304, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami]
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage explains the maxim 'The arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original' (وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل). It is applied to a case where a person removes a female gazelle from the sanctuary. After removal, she gives birth and both die. The person is liable for the compensation of both. However, if he pays the compensation before the birth, and then she gives birth and dies, he is not liable for the offspring. The reason is that the compensation payment (the substitute) is equivalent to returning the original to the sanctuary, which restores the protective status. The ruling demonstrates that payment of the substitute has the same effect as restoring the original.

Key Terms
الخلف (al-khalaf): The substitute or replacement, in this context the compensation (jaza') paid for the game.
الأصل (al-aṣl): The original, in this context the actual game being returned to the sanctuary.
وصول (wuṣūl): The arrival or reaching, indicating fulfillment of the obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim, if a person pays compensation for a female gazelle taken from the sanctuary before she gives birth, what is the ruling on the offspring if they later die?
A) The person is liable for compensation for the offspring
B) The person is not liable for compensation for the offspring
C) The person must return the offspring to the sanctuary if alive
D) The person must pay double compensation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'wuṣūl al-khalaf ka-wuṣūl al-aṣl' establishes that fulfilling an obligation through a substitute legally stands in for the original, ending further liability.

Substitute Reaches Like Original
Introduces the rule 'substitute reaches like original' with a case from hunting in Haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل' to determine liability for compensation of game in the Haram.

Core Idea
Payment of compensation substitutes for returning game to the Haram, lifting protection and liability.

In classical Hanafi fiqh, game animals in the Haram enjoy a special legal protection (amn). Even if removed, they remain protected until compensation is paid. This lesson examines the maxim 'وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل' through a case from al-Hidayah: a person removes a pregnant gazelle from the Haram, and both die. You will learn how paying compensation before birth extinguishes liability for the offspring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is removing a protected game animal from the Haram. The ruling is that the person must pay compensation (jaza') for the mother and any offspring born before compensation is paid.
The mother's protection extends to her offspring.
2
Locate the Effective Cause
The cause is the legal protection (amn) that persists even after removal. This attribute extends to the offspring.
Protection continues until compensation is paid.
3
Apply the Maxim
The payment of compensation (substitute) is legally equivalent to returning the animal to the Haram. Once paid, the protection ends.
وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل.
4
Conclude the Liability
Offspring born after compensation are not compensable because the protection was lifted by the substitute.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Some schools may not accept this equation; Hanafis base it on istihsan.
The Hanafi position is makhtalaf fih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَخْرَجَ ظَبْيَةَ الْحَرَمِ فَوَلَدَتْ فَمَاتَا ضَمِنَهُمَا فَإِنْ أَدَّى جَزَاء هَا فَوَلَدَتْ لَا يَضُمَنُ الْوَلَدَ) لأنَّ الصَّيْدَ بَعْدَ الْإِخْرَاجِ مِنْ الْحَرَمِ بَقِيَ مُسْتَحَقَّ الْأَمْنِ شَرُعًا وَلِهَذَا وَجَبَ رَدُّهُ إِلَى مَأْمَنِهِ، وَهَذِهِ صِفَةٌ شَرْعِيَّةٌ فَتَسْرِى إِلَى الْوَلَدِ فَإِنْ أَدَّى جَزَاء هَا ثُمَّ وَلَدَتْ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ جَزَاءُ الْوَلَدِ، لِأَنَّ بَعْدَ أَدَاءِ الْجَرَاءِ لَمْ تَبْقَ آمِنَةً، لَّانَّ وُصُولَ الْخَلَفِ كَوُصُولِ الْأَصْلِ.
(۲۲۰) إِنَّ وُصُولَ الْخَلْفِ كَوُصُول الأصل.
ترجمہ : بدل کا پہنچ جانا اصل کے پہنچنے کی مانند ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نائب کا پہنچ جانا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ اصل پہنچ گیا ، اور جو حکم اصل کے پہنچنے کی صورت میں مرتب ہو گا وہی حکم بدل کے پہنچنے کی صورت میں بھی دائر ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے ہرن کو حرم سے باہر نکالا ، پھر اس ہرن نے بچے جنے اور ہرن بھی مر گئی اور اس کے بچے بھی مر گئے تو اس نکالنے والے پر ان کی جزاء واجب ہوگی، کیونکہ ہرن حرم سے نکالے جانے کے بعد بھی شرعا مستحق امن ہے،اسی وجہ سے اس کو اس کی جاہ امن میں لے جانا واجب ہے، ہاں اگر اس نکالنے والے نے ہرن کی جزاء ادا کر دی پھر اس نے جنا تو اس پر بچوں کی جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ جزاء ادا کرنے کے بعد و مستحق امن نہ رہی، کیونکہ بدل یعنی قیمت کا فقراء کی طرف پہنچ جانا ایسا ہی ہے جیسا کہ ہرن کا حرم میں پہنچ جانا، اس لئے کہ اصول ہے کہ وصول بدل وصول اصل کی مانند ہوتا ہے۔
He removed a female gazelle from the Haram, and she gave birth, and both died; he is liable for their compensation. If he paid compensation for her and then she gave birth, he is not liable for the compensation of the offspring. Because after being removed from the Haram, the game remains legally entitled to safety, and therefore it is obligatory to return it to its safe place. This is a legal attribute, so it extends to the offspring. If he paid compensation for her and then she gave birth, he is not liable for compensation of the offspring, because after paying compensation she no longer remained protected, for the arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original. (220) Indeed, the arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original. Translation: The arrival of the replacement is like the arrival of the original. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that the arrival of the deputy is as if the original arrived, and whatever ruling would apply if the original arrived will also apply when the substitute arrives. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a person removed a deer from the Haram, then the deer gave birth and both died, he owes compensation for both, because even after removal, the deer is legally entitled to safety, so it must be returned. However, if he paid the compensation for the deer and then it gave birth, he does not owe compensation for the offspring, because after paying compensation the deer is no longer protected, since the delivery of the substitute (the value to the poor) is like the delivery of the original (the deer to the Haram).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim from al-Hidayah: 'The arrival of the substitute is like the arrival of the original.' The commentary explains this principle through a case in Hajj: A person removes a pregnant gazelle from the Haram (the sacred precinct). The gazelle and its offspring die. Under Hanafi law, the gazelle retained its sanctity even outside the Haram, so the person must pay compensation (jaza') for both the mother and the offspring if they die before compensation is paid. However, if the person first pays the compensation (which goes to the poor) and then the gazelle gives birth and dies, no compensation is owed for the offspring. Why? Because the payment of compensation (the substitute) to the poor is legally equivalent to returning the animal to the Haram (the original). Once the compensation is paid, the animal's protection (amn) is lifted, so any offspring born after that are not protected. This maxim is used in Hanafi fiqh to establish that certain monetary substitutes (e.g., dam, fidyah) can stand in for the actual protected object, thereby changing legal status.

Key Terms
الخلف (al-khalaf): The substitute or replacement, in this context the monetary compensation (jaza') paid for the game.
الأصل (al-asl): The original object of protection, here the game animal in the Haram.
الجزاء (al-jaza'): Compensation or expiation for killing game in the Haram or while in ihram, usually by slaughtering a similar animal or feeding the poor.
الأمن (al-amn): Legal protection or safety granted to game within the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim 'وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل', what happens to liability for offspring born after compensation is paid for the mother game?
A) Liability remains for offspring as well.
B) No liability for offspring because compensation substitutes for the original.
C) Liability is reduced by half.
D) Offspring become owned by the compensator.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'وصول الخلف كوصول الأصل' establishes that compensation lifts legal protection for game in the Haram, extinguishing liability for subsequent offspring.
