Prohibition Does Not Prevent Actuality
Explains the usul principle that prohibition does not invalidate acts, illustrated by a Makkan combining Hajj and Umrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that prohibition does not invalidate an act, and apply it to the case of a Makkan combining Hajj and Umrah.

Core Idea
An act can be valid and prohibited at the same time — prohibition does not undo actuality.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi usul principle with a concrete fiqh application. The principle that prohibition does not prevent the actuality of an act distinguishes between the validity (sihhah) of an act and its prohibition (hurma). The author of al-Hidayah uses the case of a Makkan pilgrim who combines Hajj and Umrah to illustrate this.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Learn the principle: 'Prohibition does not prevent the actuality of the act.' This means a prohibited act still legally occurs if performed.
The Arabic phrase is 'النَّهَى لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْلِ'.
2
Identify the case
The case is a Makkan (resident of Mecca) who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram (qiran).
For a Makkan, qiran is makruh tahrimi (prohibited).
3
Apply the principle
Despite the prohibition, the acts of Hajj and Umrah are valid because they were performed as intended. Prohibition does not negate actuality.
Validity (sihhah) and prohibition (hurma) are independent.
4
Determine the consequence
Because the combination is prohibited, a dam (sacrifice) is wajib (obligatory). It is a dam jabr (compulsory) from which the pilgrim may not eat.
Compare with an afaqi (pilgrim from outside Miqat) who performs qiran: his dam is dam shukr, from which he may eat.
5
Compare rulings
The difference in the type of dam shows how the legal character changes based on the pilgrim's origin and the nature of the prohibition.
Afaqi's qiran is not prohibited, so his dam is a thanksgiving sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٢٢١) إِنَّ النَّهَى لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْل. ترجمہ: نہی فعل کے تحقق کو منع نہیں کرتی ۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب کسی فعل پر نہی وارد ہو تو یہ نہی فعلِ منہی عنہ کو تحقق سے نہیں روک سکتی ، یعنی اگر اس نے فعل منہی عنہ کا ارتکاب کر لیا تو متحقق ہو جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مکی آدمی اگر حج اور عمرے کے افعال کو سرانجام دے تو یہ عبادات ادا ہو جائیں گی، کیونکہ اس نے اسی طرح ادا کیا ہے جس طرح اپنے او پر التزام کیا تھا، لیکن مکی کے لئے یہ دونوں یکجا کرنا منہی عنہ ہیں اور نہی فعل منہی عنہ کے تحقیق سے مانع نہیں ہے، لہذا مکی کا یہ حج اور عمرہ ادا ہو جائے گا، البتہ منہی عنہ کے ارتکاب کی وجہ سے اس پر دم واجب ہو گا۔
الهداية كتاب الحج، باب إضافة الإحرام ، ج ۱ ص ۳۱۰، ط: رحمانیه
(فَلَوْ أَتَمَّهُمَا أَى الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ (صَحْ) لِأَنَّهُ أَدَّى أَفْعَالَهُمَا كَمَا الْتَزَمَهُمَا غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ مَنْهِيٌّ عَنْهُ وَالنَّهَى لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْلِ كَمَا فِي الْإِصْلَاحِ وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ) لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَهُوَ دَمُ جَبُرٍ لَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ مِنْهُ بِخِلَافِ الْآفَاقِى حَيْثُ يَجُوزُ لَهُ الْأَكُلُ، لِأَنَّهُ دَمُ شُكْرٍ.
(221) Indeed, prohibition does not prevent the actuality of the act. Translation: Prohibition does not prevent the actualization of the act. Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that when a prohibition is issued on an act, this prohibition cannot prevent the actualization of the prohibited act, meaning if he commits the prohibited act, it will be actualized. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a Makkan person performs the acts of Hajj and Umrah, these acts of worship will be valid, because he performed them as he committed himself to do, but for the Makkan, combining these two is prohibited, and prohibition does not prevent the actualization of the prohibited act. Therefore, his Hajj and Umrah will be valid, but he owes a dam (slaughtering an animal) for committing the prohibited act. Al-Hidayah: Kitab al-Hajj, Bab Idafat al-Ihram, vol. 1 p. 310: 'If he completes both, meaning Hajj and Umrah, (it is valid) because he performed their acts as he committed himself to them, except that he is prohibited from that, and prohibition does not prevent the actuality of the act, as in the case of reconciliation. And he owes a dam for combining them, and it is a dam of jabar (compulsory), and he may not eat from it, unlike the afaqi (outsider) who may eat from his dam because it is a dam of thanks.'
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage presents the principle 'Prohibition does not prevent actuality' (النَّهَى لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْلِ). The commentary explains that when an act is prohibited, the prohibition does not make the act impossible or invalid if performed; the act still takes place and is legally recognized as occurring. The author of al-Hidayah applies this to a Makkan (resident of Mecca) who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram. According to Hanafi law, a Makkan is prohibited from combining Hajj and Umrah (i.e., performing 'qiran') because he is not a traveler; for him, the recommended form is ifrad (Hajj alone). However, if he nevertheless performs both, his Hajj and Umrah are valid (sahih). He has fulfilled what he intended, despite the prohibition. The consequence is that he must offer a dam (sacrifice) as a penalty (dam jabar), and he is not allowed to eat from it, because it is a compulsory sacrifice. In contrast, an afaqi (a pilgrim from outside Mecca) who performs Hajj and Umrah together (qiran) also owes a dam, but his is a dam shukr (thanksgiving), from which he may eat. This distinction shows that the legal character of the dam differs based on the pilgrim's origin and the nature of the prohibition.

Key Terms
النَّهَى (al-nahy): A prohibition or forbiddance from an act; in usul al-fiqh, a demand to abstain.
تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْل (tahaqquq al-fi'l): The actualization or real occurrence of the act; the act is considered to have been performed legally.
دَمُ جَبُرٍ (damu jabar): A compulsory or penalty sacrifice, as opposed to a voluntary thanksgiving sacrifice. The person may not eat from it.
دَمُ شُكْرٍ (damu shukr): A thanksgiving sacrifice; the offerer may eat from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Makkan combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The pilgrimage is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The pilgrimage is valid but he must offer a dam and cannot eat from it.
C) The pilgrimage is valid and no penalty is required.
D) Only the Umrah is valid, the Hajj is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Prohibition does not invalidate an act; validity and prohibition can coexist, with penalties for the prohibition.

Sanctity of Property Like Sanctity of Life
States a foundational legal maxim equating property and life sanctity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'Inna hurmat al-mal kahurmat al-nafs' and apply it to identify when destroying or harming another's property is legally prohibited.

Core Idea
Property is inviolable: unjust destruction of wealth is as forbidden as taking a life.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle from Al-Hidayah that equates the sanctity of wealth with that of life. Understanding this maxim is key to Hanafi rulings on financial trusts, liability for damages, and the limits of permissible expenditure. We will define the maxim, explore its scope, and see how it applies to everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
Read the Arabic phrase 'إن حرمة المال كحرمة النفس' and commit it to memory. It means 'Indeed, the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life.'
This is a qa'ida kulliya (universal maxim) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Define the key terms
Analyze 'hurmat al-mal' (sanctity of property) and 'hurmat al-nafs' (sanctity of life). Understand that both entail protection from unjust harm.
The word 'hurma' implies a sacred inviolability, not just social respect.
3
Determine the legal implication
The maxim establishes that destroying or harming another's property without right is haram, just like murder. It creates a general prohibition but allows exceptions for legal grounds like necessity or authorized taking.
Exceptions must be supported by specific evidence (e.g., compensation, public interest).
4
Apply to a concrete case
Consider a scenario where someone deliberately breaks a neighbor's window without cause. Apply the maxim: the act is haram and requires compensation (daman).
The ruling for murder is similar: haram and requires qisas/diya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۲۲) إِنَّ حُرُمَةَ الْمَالِ كَحُرُمَةِ النَّفْسِ .
ترجمہ : مال کی حرمت جان کی حرمت کی طرح ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس طرح مسلمان کی جان محفوظ ہے اور جان کو ضائع کرنا حرام ہے اسی طرح مال کو ضائع کرنا بھی حرام ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ محصر آدمی اگر حج کو پا سکتا ہو لیکن

Explanation: The meaning of the mentioned principle is that just as a Muslim's life is protected and it is haram to destroy it, similarly destroying wealth is also haram. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that a person who is blocked (from proceeding with Hajj) - if he can reach (complete) Hajj... but [incomplete].

Commentary
This passage introduces the legal maxim: 'The sanctity of property is like the sanctity of life' (إن حرمة المال كحرمة النفس). The Urdu commentary explains that just as it is forbidden to take the life of a Muslim without right, it is also forbidden to destroy or harm his property without legal justification. This principle is foundational in Hanafi fiqh for protecting financial rights and property from aggression. The text then states that the author of al-Hidayah uses this principle to discuss the case of a muhsar (one who is prevented from completing Hajj), but the explanation is cut off in the available pages. Based on typical Hidayah rulings, this maxim would apply to situations where the muhsar must safeguard his wealth and cannot be forced to spend beyond necessity. The principle also underlies rulings on unlawful takings (ghasb), destruction of property, and financial compensations.

Key Terms
حُرْمَةُ الْمَالِ (hurmat al-mal): The inviolability or sanctity of wealth; property is legally protected from seizure or destruction without cause.
النَّفْس (al-nafs): Life or the self; here meaning the sanctity of a Muslim's life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is makruh but not haram.
B) It is haram, just like taking a life.
C) It is permissible if compensation is paid later.
D) It is only blameworthy if the property is of great value.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'hurmat al-mal kahurmat al-nafs' establishes that property is inviolable, and unjust harm to it is as forbidden as harm to life itself.

Prohibition Does Not Invalidate: The Hanafi Maxim Debated
Explains a legal maxim with application to Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-nahy la yamna' tahaqquq al-fi'l' to determine that a prohibited act in Hajj remains valid and identify the compensatory obligation (dam jabar).

Core Idea
A prohibited act is still valid; prohibition only incurs compensation, not invalidity.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani explains a key Hanafi legal maxim: a prohibition does not prevent the actual occurrence of the prohibited act. This means that even if an action is forbidden (e.g., combining Hajj and Umrah for a Meccan resident), if performed, it is still valid (sahih) as a real act of worship. The prohibition only necessitates a compensatory sacrifice (dam jabar). This principle distinguishes between legal invalidity (batil) and mere prohibition (haram), a crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
Determine the act in question: a Meccan combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram.
The actor is a Meccan, i.e., a resident within the Miqat boundaries.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the text, the act is valid (sahih) even though prohibited.
Validity is independent of prohibition.
3
Locate the governing maxim
The ruling is based on the maxim: 'النهي لا يمنع تحقق الفعل' (Prohibition does not prevent actualization).
This is a general principle in Hanafi usul.
4
Understand the rationale
The acts are performed as the person obligated himself; the prohibition does not affect their legal existence.
The act is real (tahaqquq) even if sinful.
5
Determine the consequence
The compensatory dam (dam jabar) is obligatory, which the offeror cannot eat from.
Contrast with dam shukr for afaqi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إضافة الإحرام
(٢٢١) إِنَّ النَّهَى لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْل. ترجمہ: نہی فعل کے تحقق کو منع نہیں کرتی ۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب کسی فعل پر نہی وارد ہو تو یہ نہی فعلِ منہی عنہ کو تحقق سے نہیں روک سکتی ، یعنی اگر اس نے فعل منہی عنہ کا ارتکاب کر لیا تو متحقق ہو جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ مکی آدمی اگر حج اور عمرے کے افعال کو سرانجام دے تو یہ عبادات ادا ہو جائیں گی، کیونکہ اس نے اسی طرح ادا کیا ہے جس طرح اپنے او پر التزام کیا تھا، لیکن مکی کے لئے یہ دونوں یکجا کرنا منہی عنہ ہیں اور نہی فعل منہی عنہ کے تحقیق سے مانع نہیں ہے، لہذا مکی کا یہ حج اور عمرہ ادا ہو جائے گا، البتہ منہی عنہ کے ارتکاب کی وجہ سے اس پر دم واجب ہو گا۔
فَلَوْ أَتَمَّهُمَا أَى الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ صَحَّ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَّى أَفْعَالَهُمَا كَمَا الْتَزَمَهُمَا غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ مَنْهِيٌّ عَنْهُ وَالنَّهَى لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْلِ كَمَا فِي الْإِصْلَاحِ وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَهُوَ دَمُ جَبُرٍ لَا يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ مِنْهُ بِخِلَافِ الْآفَاقِى حَيْثُ يَجُوزُ لَهُ الْأَكُلُ لِأَنَّهُ دَمُ شُكْرٍ.
Section: Adding Ihram. (221) Indeed, prohibition does not prevent the realization of the act. Translation: Prohibition does not prevent the occurrence of the act. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that when a prohibition comes upon an act, this prohibition cannot prevent the prohibited act from occurring, meaning if he commits the prohibited act, it will be realized. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a Meccan person performs the acts of Hajj and Umrah, these acts of worship will be valid, because he performed them as he had obligated himself, but for the Meccan, combining both is prohibited, and prohibition does not prevent the realization of the prohibited act, so his Hajj and Umrah will be valid, however, due to committing the prohibited act, a dam (blood sacrifice) becomes obligatory upon him. So if he completes both, i.e., Hajj and Umrah, it is valid because he performed their acts as he obligated himself, except that he is prohibited from it, and prohibition does not prevent the realization of the act as in al-Islah, and upon him is a dam because of combining them, and it is a dam of jabar (compensation) from which he is not allowed to eat, unlike the afaqi (one from outside the Miqat) where he is allowed to eat because it is a dam of gratitude.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting a legal maxim (qa'ida) from Al-Hidayah: 'Prohibition does not prevent the actualization of the act.' The author of the Urdu commentary explains that when a prohibition is issued on an act, it does not render the act impossible; if one performs it, the act occurs as a real event. The application is to a Meccan (resident of the Haram) who performs Hajj and Umrah together. Although combining them is prohibited for the Meccan, the acts are still valid because he performed them as he intended. The prohibition does not invalidate; it only incurs a compensatory dam (blood sacrifice). The Arabic quote from Al-Hidayah confirms: if he completes both, it is valid, but he owes a dam of jabar (compensation) which he cannot eat from, unlike an afaqi (one from outside) who can eat from his dam of gratitude. This highlights the Hanafi principle that validity and prohibition are independent matters.

Key Terms
نَهَى (nahy): A legal prohibition that makes an act sinful but does not necessarily invalidate it.
تَحَقَّقَ الْفِعْل (tahaqquq al-fi'l): The actual occurrence of the act as a real entity, regardless of its legal status.
دَم جَبُر (dam jabar): A compensatory blood sacrifice required for violating a prohibition in Hajj, from which the offeror may not eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Meccan performs Hajj and Umrah together. According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of his pilgrimage?
A) Invalid because it is prohibited
B) Valid, but he must offer a compensatory dam
C) Valid and no penalty
D) Invalid unless he performs it separately

Key Takeaway
A prohibited act in Hanafi fiqh is still valid; the prohibition merely triggers a compensatory obligation, not nullification.

The Principle of Wealth Inviolability and Its Application to Ihsaar
Explaining the principle and its application to ihsar via istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that wealth has sanctity equal to life, and apply it to the case of a muhsar to determine the permissibility of tahlul by istihsan.

Core Idea
Wealth is inviolable like life; preserving wealth can justify exiting ihram by istihsan, even without life threat.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes a major legal maxim: the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. The author then applies this maxim to the situation of a person prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar) who can reach Mecca but cannot afford the sacrificial animal (hady). Strict analogy would require going to Mecca, but that would waste his wealth. By istihsan (juristic preference), he may exit ihram to preserve his wealth, though proceeding to Mecca remains better.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Extract the maxim 'hurmat al-mal ka hurmat al-nafs' from the text. Understand that wasting wealth is prohibited just as wasting life is.
2
Recognize the Case
The case is a muhsar who can physically reach Hajj but cannot reach the hady (sacrificial animal). This creates a dilemma: if he goes, his wealth is wasted; if he does not go, he remains in ihram indefinitely.
3
Understand the Conflict
Strict analogy (qiyas) would require him to go to Mecca because he can reach it. But this would cause financial loss against the principle that wealth is inviolable.
4
Apply Istihsan
Istihsan sets aside strict analogy in favor of a more equitable ruling: to prevent waste of wealth, the muhsar may make tahlul (exit ihram). This is like the case where one fears for his life.
5
Note the Better Option
The text states that proceeding to Mecca and performing Hajj is afdal (better) if possible. Istihsan provides a concession, not a preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحصار
(٢٢٢) إِنَّ حُرُمَةَ الْمَالِ كَحُرُمَةِ النَّفْسِ .
ترجمہ: مال کی حرمت جان کی حرمت کی طرح ہے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جس طرح مسلمان کی جان محفوظ ہے اور جان کو ضائع کرنا حرام ہے اسی طرح مال کو ضائع کرنا بھی حرام ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ محصر آدمی اگر حج کو پا سکتا ہو لیکن ہدی کو نہ پاسکتا ہو تو اس کے لئے استحسانا حلال ہونا جائز ہے، تاہم افضل یہ ہے کہ مکہ چلا جائے اور افعال حج کو اداء کر لے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس محصر کے ذمہ مکہ جانا لازم کر دیں تو اس صورت میں اس کا مال ضائع ہو جائے گا اور چونکہ مال کی حرمت نفس کی حرمت کی طرح ہے، اس لئے یہ استحسانا حلال ہوسکتا ہے۔
وَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَتَحَلَّلْ يَضِيعُ مَالُهُ مَجَّانًا، وَحُرْمَةُ الْمَالِ كَحُرُمَةِ النَّفْسِ فَيَتَحَلَّلُ كَمَا إِذَا خَافَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ، وَالْأَفْضَلُ أَنْ يَتَوَجَّهَ.
Section: Ihsaar (being prevented from completing Hajj). (222) Indeed, the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. Translation: The sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that just as a Muslim's life is protected and wasting life is forbidden, similarly wasting wealth is forbidden. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that if a person prevented (muhsar) can reach Hajj but cannot reach the sacrificial animal (hady), then for him, making tahlul (leaving ihram) is permissible by istihsan, however, it is better to go to Mecca and perform the acts of Hajj. The reason for istihsan is that if we make it necessary for this muhsar to go to Mecca, then his wealth would be wasted, and since the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life, therefore he may make tahlul by istihsan. The rationale for istihsan is that if he does not make tahlul, his wealth will be wasted for nothing, and the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life, so he may make tahlul just as when he fears for his life, and it is better to proceed (to Mecca).
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting a legal maxim from Al-Hidayah: 'The sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life.' The commentator explains that just as a Muslim's life is inviolable, so is his wealth; wasting either is haram. The application is to a person prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj who can reach Hajj but cannot reach the sacrificial animal (hady). If going to Mecca would cause his wealth to be wasted, then by istihsan (juristic preference) he is allowed to exit ihram (tahlul) to preserve his wealth. However, it is afdal (better) to proceed to Mecca and perform Hajj. The Arabic quote from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq provides the istihsan reasoning: if he does not make tahlul, his wealth will be wasted for nothing, and since wealth is sacred like life, he may make tahlul just as he would if his life were in danger. This illustrates how istihsan operates to prevent hardship and loss of wealth.

Key Terms
حُرُمَة الْمَال (hurmat al-mal): The inviolability and protection of a person's wealth; wasting it is prohibited.
اسْتِحْسَان (istihsan): A juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy for a more equitable ruling based on a stronger evidence.
مُحْصَر (muhsar): A person who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah after entering ihram due to an obstacle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in this passage, what is the ruling for a muhsar who can reach Hajj but cannot reach the hady?
A) He must sacrifice an animal anyway
B) He may exit ihram by istihsan to avoid wasting wealth
C) He must continue regardless
D) He must send money to Mecca

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that wealth is inviolable like life, so a muhsar may exit ihram by istihsan to avoid wasting wealth, even if his life is not in danger.

The Hanafi Position on Umrah: Sunnah Not Fard
Arguing that Umrah is sunnah, not fard, due to conflicting evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on Umrah, apply the principle that conflicting athar prevent fardiyyah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on Quran 2:196.

Core Idea
Conflict in transmitted reports prevents establishing a definitive obligation; thus Umrah remains sunnah.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: whether Umrah is obligatory (fard) or recommended (sunnah). The Hanafi school argues that because there are conflicting reports (athar) regarding Umrah's status, fardiyyah cannot be established. The opposing view, held by Imam al-Shafi'i, relies on the Quranic verse that joins Umrah with Hajj and commands completion. By the end, you will understand the Ḥanafī principle that fard requires decisive proof and how this principle resolves the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
State the contested ruling: Is Umrah fard or sunnah? Recognize that the dispute centers on the legal nature of Umrah.
Disagreement between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its basis
The Hanafi school holds Umrah is sunnah. The basis is the principle that fardiyyah is not established when athar conflict. Identify the Quranic evidence used by the Shafi'is and the Hanafi response.
Fard requires decisive proof (qat'i); conflicting reports prevent this.
3
Analyze the opposing evidence
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: Quran 2:196 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah.' They argue that conjunction of Umrah with Hajj and the command (amr) for ithmam indicates obligation.
The amr is for 'ithmam', which only applies after starting.
4
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: (1) Conjunction in wording does not necessitate conjunction in ruling. (2) The command to 'complete' (ithmam) only applies after one has already begun the act. Thus it does not prove initial obligation.
Hanafis agree that once started, Umrah becomes wajib to complete, but initially it is sunnah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference: Hanafis view Umrah as sunnah (recommended, can be performed multiple times without obligation), while Shafi'is view it as fard (obligatory once in a lifetime).
This affects the legal weight of starting and completing Umrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الفوات
(٢٢٣) إِنَّ الْفَرْضِيَّةَ لَا تَثْبُتُ مَعَ التَّعَارُضِ فِي الْآثَارِ.
ترجمہ: آثار میں تعارض کے ہوتے ہوئے فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔
تشریح : مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جب کسی کے بارے میں دو نصوص یا آثار میں تعارض آجائے تو اس سے فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ عمرہ احناف کے نزدیک سنت ہے فرض نہیں ہے، کیونکہ عمرے کے بارے میں دو نصوص آپس میں متعارض ہیں اور نصوص میں تعارض کے ہوتے ہوئے فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ، اس لئے کہ فرضیت دلیل قطعی سے ثابت ہوتی ہے۔
وَإِذَا تَعَارَضَتْ الْآثَارُ لَا تَنْبُتُ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلَّا بِدَلِيلِ مَقْطُوعِ بِهِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: هُوَ ثَابِتٌ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ عَطَفَ الْعُمْرَةَ عَلَى الْحَقِّ، وَالْحَجُّ فَرِيضَةٌ، وَأَمَرَ بِالْإِثْمَامِ وَالأمْرُ لِلْوُجُوبِ أُجِيبَ بِأَنَّ الْقِرَانَ فِي النَّظْمِ لَا يُوجِبُ الْقِرَانَ فِي الْحُكْمِ، وَالْأَمْرُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِالْإِثْمَامِ، وَالْإِثْمَامُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بَعْدَ الشُّرُوعِ، وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ بِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ سُنَّةً.
Section: Fawat (missing Hajj). (223) Indeed, fardiyyah (obligatory nature) is not established with conflict in the reports (athar). Translation: Obligatory status is not established when there is conflict in the reports. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that when there is conflict between two texts or reports about something, then from that conflict fardiyyah cannot be established. The author of Hidayah mentions this principle to explain that among the Hanafis, Umrah is sunnah, not fard, because there are two conflicting texts regarding Umrah, and with conflict among texts, fardiyyah cannot be established, because fardiyyah is established only by a decisive proof. And when reports conflict, fardiyyah does not arise, because it is only established by decisive evidence. If it is said: It is established by the saying of Allah Most High: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (Quran 2:196) – He joined Umrah to Hajj, and Hajj is fard, and He commanded completion, and a command indicates obligation. The answer is: Joining in phrasing does not necessitate joining in ruling, and the command is only for completion (ithmam), and completion is only after commencement, and we say that (i.e., Umrah becomes wajib after commencement) even though in the beginning it is sunnah.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It presents the principle: 'Fardiyyah is not established when reports conflict.' The author explains that when there are conflicting texts about a matter, obligation cannot be proven, because obligation requires definitive proof. The Hanafi ruling that Umrah is sunnah (recommended), not fard (obligatory), is based on this principle. The opposing view argues that the Quranic verse 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (2:196) joins Umrah with Hajj, implying Umrah is also obligatory. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) Conjunction in the text does not require conjunction in legal ruling; Hajj is fard, but Umrah can be different. (2) The command is to complete (ithmam), which only applies after one has already started; thus it does not prove initial obligation. The Hanafis accept that once one begins Umrah, it becomes wajib to complete, but initially it is sunnah. This illustrates the Hanafi usul that conflicting athar prevent a ruling of fard, and that Umrah is not established as fard due to this conflict.

Key Terms
فَرْضِيَّة (fardiyyah): The quality of being obligatory (fard) – a ruling that is established by a decisive proof (qat'i).
تَعَارُض فِي الْآثَار (ta'arud fi al-athar): Conflict or apparent contradiction between two transmitted reports or texts regarding a legal issue.
إِثْمَام (ithmam): Completion of an act after having started it; in this context, completing Hajj or Umrah after ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the Hanafis consider Umrah as sunnah rather than fard?
A) Lack of any Quranic mention
B) Conflicting evidence among reports prevents establishing fard
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) The word 'Umrah' does not appear in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Fardiyyah requires decisive proof; conflicting athar prevent establishing obligation, hence Umrah is sunnah initially.

Conflicting Texts Prevent Establishing Obligation
Ruling with proof: 'Umrah is sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why conflicting transmitted reports prevent establishing the fardiyyah (obligation) of 'Umrah in the Hanafi school and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i counter-argument using the verse.

Core Idea
Conflicting reports block definitive obligation; 'Umrah is sunnah because the Qur'an commands completion, not initiation.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi legal principle: when transmitted evidences (athar) conflict, a ruling of obligation (fardiyyah) cannot be established because obligation requires definitive proof. The passage applies this principle to the status of 'Umrah, contrasting the Hanafi view that 'Umrah is sunnah with the Shafi'i view that it is fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The passage states: 'Indeed, obligation is not established with conflict in the transmitted reports.' This is a foundational Hanafi rule: fardiyyah requires qat'i (definitive) proof; conflicting athar prevent that certainty.
Hanafi usul holds that obligation (fard) must be based on qat'i dalil; zanni evidence yields wajib or less.
2
Locate the dalil
The verse cited is Qur'an 2:196: 'And complete the Hajj and the 'Umrah for Allah.' The Shafi'i school uses this verse, claiming the conjunctive structure makes 'Umrah equal to Hajj in obligation.
The conjunction 'wa' (and) does not automatically equate legal rulings, as the Hanafi response clarifies.
3
Understand the opponent's argument
The opponent (Imam al-Shafi'i) argues: (a) 'Umrah is conjuncted to Hajj, which is fard, so 'Umrah is also fard; (b) the imperative 'atimmu' indicates obligation.
The Shafi'i position is that 'Umrah is wajib (fard) once in a lifetime.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) Conjunction in wording (qiran fi al-nazm) does not require conjunction in ruling (qiran fi al-hukm). (2) The command 'atimmu' is specifically for completion (ithmam) after commencement, not for initiating the act. The Hanafis agree that once started, 'Umrah becomes wajib, but initially it is sunnah.
This is a classic example of tamyiz al-dalalah — distinguishing the scope of the command.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'is must perform 'Umrah once in a lifetime as an obligation; Hanafis consider it a highly recommended sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) that becomes wajib only after starting.
This affects pilgrimage planning and legal liability (e.g., sin for omitting a fard vs. no sin for omitting a sunnah if never started).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الفوات (٢٢٣) إِنَّ الْفَرْضِيَّةَ لَا تَثْبُتُ مَعَ التَّعَارُضِ فِي الْآثَارِ.
وَإِذَا تَعَارَضَتْ الْآثَارُ لَا تَنْبُتُ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَثْبُتُ إِلَّا بِدَلِيلِ مَقْطُوعِ بِهِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: هُوَ ثَابِتٌ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ عَطَفَ الْعُمْرَةَ عَلَى الْحَقِّ، وَالْحَجُّ فَرِيضَةٌ، وَأَمَرَ بِالْإِثْمَامِ وَالأمْرُ لِلْوُجُوبِ أُجِيبَ بِأَنَّ الْقِرَانَ فِي النَّظْمِ لَا يُوجِبُ الْقِرَانَ فِي الْحُكْمِ، وَالْأَمْرُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ بِالْإِثْمَامِ، وَالْإِثْمَامُ إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بَعْدَ الشُّرُوعِ، وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ بِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ سُنَّةً.
تبيين الحقائق: كتاب الحج، باب إضافة الإحرام ، ج ٢ ص ٨١، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي] الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الفوات، ج ١ ص ٣١٦، ط: رحمانيه
Section on al-Fawat. (223) Indeed, obligation is not established with conflict in the transmitted reports. And when reports conflict, obligation is not established because it is only established by a definitive proof. If it is said: It is established by His statement, the Exalted, 'And complete the Hajj and the 'Umrah for Allah' – conjuncting 'Umrah to Hajj, and Hajj is an obligation, and He commanded with completion, and the command is for obligation. The answer is: Conjunction in wording does not necessitate conjunction in ruling, and the command is only for completion, and completion only occurs after commencement, and we affirm it even if at the beginning it is a sunnah.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the chapter on al-Fawat (missed acts) of Hajj. The passage states a foundational principle: when transmitted evidences (athar) conflict, an obligation (fardiyyah) cannot be established, because obligation requires a definitive (qat'i) proof. The commentator then applies this to the ruling of 'Umrah. An opponent argues that the Qur'anic verse 'And complete the Hajj and the 'Umrah for Allah' (al-Baqarah 2:196) makes 'Umrah obligatory because (a) 'Umrah is conjuncted to Hajj, which is a fard, and (b) the command 'atimmu' (complete) is an imperative indicating obligation. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) grammatical conjunction (al-qiran fi al-nazm) does not require equality in legal ruling (al-hukm); (2) the command is specifically for completion (ithmam) after beginning the act, not for initiating it as an obligation. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that 'Umrah is a sunnah at its commencement, though it becomes necessary once begun. This principle explains why conflicting reports on 'Umrah's legal status prevent it from being fard.

Key Terms
فَرْضِيَّة (fardiyyah): The quality or state of being an obligation (fard) in Islamic law.
تَعَارُض (ta'āruḍ): Conflict or apparent contradiction between two or more transmitted evidences (athar), precluding establishment of a definitive ruling.
آثَار (āthār): Transmitted reports, including hadith and other narrations, serving as evidence in deriving rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because 'Umrah is only mentioned in weak hadiths.
D) Because the majority of scholars say so.

Key Takeaway
Conflicting transmitted reports prevent establishing a definitive obligation; thus 'Umrah is sunnah (becoming wajib only after commencement).

Agent's Act Contrary to Command Is Personal
Ruling on agent's violation in delegated Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when an agent violates the principal's specific command in a delegated act (like Hajj), the act is attributed to the agent, not the principal, and explain the rational proof.

Core Idea
Disobeying the principal's specific command voids agency — the act becomes the agent's own.

In delegated acts of worship like Hajj, the agent must follow the principal's command precisely. This lesson examines a scenario where an agent is appointed by two separate principals to perform Hajj, but instead of intending each Hajj exclusively, he intends both simultaneously. The legal ruling is that this act of Hajj is not valid for either principal; instead, it becomes the agent's own Hajj. We will explore the reasoning (dalil 'aqli) behind this ruling and apply it to real situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Maxim
State the ruling: 'If a commanded person acts contrary to the command, the action is attributed to the commanded, not the commander.' This is the foundation of the case.
The maxim is general and applies to any agency where the specific command is violated.
2
Recognize the Three Scenarios
The text describes three ways the agent might enter ihram: (1) for both principals together, (2) for one without specification, (3) absolutely (without naming any). The case in the book is the first scenario, where the agent intends both simultaneously.
The other scenarios are mentioned but not detailed; focus on the first.
3
Understand Why It Cannot Be Attributed to Either Principal
Each principal commanded the agent to make his Hajj exclusive and intend it specifically. The agent's combined intention violates both commands. Since no principal has priority over the other, the act cannot be assigned to either.
This is a rational deduction: without priority, no basis to prefer one.
4
Apply the Ruling to the Case
The agent's Hajj is valid for himself (if he is Muslim and capable) but not for any principal. He cannot later transfer it to a principal because the act has already occurred as his own.
The ruling prevents retroactive assignment, ensuring the integrity of the principal's command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحج عن الغير (٢٢٤) إِنَّ فِعْلَ الْمَأْمُورِ إِذَا خَالَفَ أَمْرَ الْآمِرِ يَقَعُ عَنِ الْمَأْمُورِ لَا عَنِ الْآمِرِ.
الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الحج عن الغير، ج ١ ص ٣١٧، ط: رحمانیہ وَالْمَسْأَلَة عَلَى ثَلاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ: إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ أَحْرَمَ عَنْهُمَا جَمِيعًا، أَوْ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا غَيْرَ عَيْنٍ أَوْ أَطْلَقَ فَإِنْ نَوَاهُمَا جَمِيعًا، وَهِيَ مَسْأَلَةُ الْكِتَابِ فَقَدْ خَالَفَهُمَا لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يُخْلِصَ لَهُ الْحَجَّ وَأَنْ يَنْوِيَهُ بِعَيْنِهِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْعَلُ صَارَ مُحَالِفًا، وَلَا يَكُونُ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا ، إِذْ لَيْسَ أَحَدُهُمَا بِأَوْلَى مِنْ الْآخَرِ فَوَقَعَ عَنْ الْمَأْمُورِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُهُ أَنْ يَجْعَلَهُ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، لأَنَّهُ قَدْ وَقَعَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَى جَعْلِهِ لِغَيْرِهِ.
تبيين الحقائق كتاب الحج، باب الحج عن الغير ج ٢ ص ٨٦، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي]
Section on Hajj on behalf of another. (224) Indeed, the action of the commanded person when it contradicts the command of the commander occurs on behalf of the commanded, not on behalf of the commander. Al-Hidayah Book of Hajj, Chapter on Hajj on behalf of another, vol. 1 p. 317, Rahmani ed. And the case has three aspects: either he enters ihram for both of them together, or for one of them without specification, or absolutely. If he intends both together, which is the case in the book, then he has opposed them both, because each of them ordered him to make his Hajj exclusive and to intend it specifically at the time of ihram. If he does not do so, he becomes a violator, and it is not on behalf of either of them, since no one of them has priority over the other. So it falls on behalf of the commanded (the agent). And it is not possible for him to make it for one of them after that, because it has fallen for himself, so he cannot make it for another.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on al-Hajj 'an al-Ghayr (Hajj on behalf of another). The passage presents a legal maxim: if a commanded person (al-ma'mur) acts contrary to the command of the commander (al-amir), the action is attributed to the commanded person, not the commander. The commentator applies this to a scenario where two principals (amiran) each appoint the same agent (wakil) to perform Hajj on their behalf separately. If the agent enters ihram with the intention of performing Hajj for both simultaneously, he has violated the commands of both principals. The ruling is that this Hajj is not valid for either principal, nor can it be assigned to one of them later. Instead, the Hajj becomes the agent's own Hajj. The reason is that each principal commanded the agent to perform Hajj exclusively for him individually, by specifying the intention. The agent's combined intention contradicts that. Since neither principal has legal priority over the other, the act cannot be attributed to either, and it falls back on the agent. This is a pure logical deduction (dalil 'aqli) based on the nature of agency and command.

Key Terms
مَأْمُور (ma'mūr): The person commanded; here the agent commissioned to perform Hajj on behalf of another.
آمِر (āmir): The commander; the principal who issues the command to perform Hajj on his behalf.
وَقَعَ عَن (waqa'a 'an): To occur on behalf of; the legal attribution of an action to a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an agent's act contrary to the principal's specific command in worship becomes the agent's own act and cannot be retroactively assigned to the principal.

Act Contrary to Command Is Attributed to the Agent
States legal principle and applies to joint Hajj agency case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim regarding an agent's contrary act and apply it to cases of joint agency in Hajj and other acts.

Core Idea
An agent's act contrary to command is valid only for the agent, not the principal.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of an act performed by an agent depends on compliance with the principal's command. This lesson examines a key maxim: when an agent acts contrary to the command, the act is valid but belongs entirely to the agent. We will explore the maxim through a case of joint Hajj agency, as explained in al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Maxim and Its Condition
The maxim states: 'Indeed, the act of the commanded person, when it contradicts the command of the commander, occurs on behalf of the commanded person, not on behalf of the commander.' The key condition is a clear command and a violation of that command.
The maxim applies to any agency relationship where a specific instruction is given.
2
Apply the Maxim to the Hajj Agency Scenario
Two principals appoint an agent to perform Hajj separately for each. The agent enters ihram with the intention of performing one Hajj on behalf of both. This violates the command, as each principal required exclusive intention.
The violation is clear because the command was to intend separately.
3
Determine the Attribution of the Act
Since the agent acted contrary to the command, the Hajj is not valid on behalf of either principal. It is valid for the agent himself. The agent is liable for expenses and cannot later assign the reward.
The act cannot be split nor preference given, so it falls to the agent.
4
Confirm the Ruling's Rationale
The ruling prevents unjust enrichment and ensures that the principal's intention is respected. The agent bears the consequences of his deviation.
This rational proof (dalil aqli) is the basis for the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحج عن الغير
(٢٢٤) إِنَّ فِعْلَ الْمَأْمُورِ إِذَا خَالَفَ أَمْرَ الْآمِرِ يَقَعُ عَنِ الْمَأْمُورِ لَا عَنِ الْآمِرِ.
ترجمہ: مامور کا فعل جب آمر کے حکم کے خلاف ہو تو وہ مامور ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا نہ کہ آمر کی طرف سے۔
تشریح: مذکورہ اصول کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آمر جب مامور کو کسی کام کا حکم کرے پھر مامور آمر کے حکم کے خلاف کرے تو یہ کام مامور کی اپنی طرف سے ہوگا، یعنی اس فعل کے متعلق جتنے بھی حقوق ہیں وہ مامور کی طرف راجع ہوں گے اور آمر اس صورت میں بری ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ مذکورہ اصول ذکر کر کے یہ بتلا رہے ہیں کہ اگر دو آدمیوں نے کسی کو وکیل بنایا اس بات کا کہ وہ وکیل ان دونوں یعنی موکلین میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے الگ الگ حج کرے، پھر مامور نے دونوں کی طرف سے ایک ہی حج کا احرام باندھا تو حج اسی مامور کی طرف سے ہوگا، آمروں کی طرف سے نہ ہو گا۔ اور اس حج پر جتنا خرچہ ہوا ہے اس کا بھی یہی مامور ضامن ہو گا، اس لئے کہ مامور کا فعل آمر کے حکم کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ اس کو حکم دیا تھا کہ ہر ایک کی طرف سے الگ الگ بغیر اشتراک کے حج کرے، اب کسی کو دوسرے پر ترجیح بھی نہیں دے سکتے، اس لئے کہ ترجیح بلا مرجح لازم آئے گی، جب یہ حج دونوں کی طرف سے بھی نہیں ہوسکتا، اور کسی کو تر جیح بھی نہیں دی جاسکتی تو یہ حج مامور کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔
الهداية كتاب الحج، باب الحج عن الغير، ج ۱ ص ۳۱۷، ط: رحمانیہ: وَالْمَسْأَلَة عَلَى ثَلاثَةِ أَوْجُهِ: إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ أَحْرَمَ عَنْهُمَا جَمِيعًا، أَوْ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا غَيْرَ عَيْنٍ أَوْ أَطْلَقَ فَإِنْ نَوَاهُمَا جَمِيعًا، وَهِيَ مَسْأَلَةُ الْكِتَابِ فَقَدْ خَالَفَهُمَا لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يُخْلِصَ لَهُ الْحَجَّ وَأَنْ يَنْوِيَهُ بِعَيْنِهِ عِنْدَ الْإِحْرَامِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْعَلُ صَارَ مُحَالِفًا، وَلَا يَكُونُ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا ، إِذْ لَيْسَ أَحَدُهُمَا بِأَوْلَى مِنْ الْآخَرِ فَوَقَعَ عَنْ الْمَأْمُورِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُهُ أَنْ يَجْعَلَهُ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، لأَنَّهُ قَدْ وَقَعَ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَقْدِرُ عَلَى جَعْلِهِ لِغَيْرِهِ.
تبيين الحقائق كتاب الحج، باب الحج عن الغير ج ۲ ص ۸۶، ط: دار الكتاب الإسلامي
Chapter: Hajj on behalf of another. (224) Indeed, the act of the commanded person, when it contradicts the command of the commander, occurs on behalf of the commanded person, not on behalf of the commander. Translation: When the agent's act is contrary to the principal's command, it is valid on behalf of the agent, not the principal. Explanation: The meaning of the aforementioned principle is that when the principal commands the agent to do something, then the agent acts contrary to the principal's command, this act will be on behalf of the agent himself; that is, all rights related to this act will revert to the agent, and the principal will be absolved in this case. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle and explains that if two persons appoint an agent to perform Hajj separately on behalf of each of them, but the agent entered ihram for one Hajj on behalf of both, then the Hajj is valid on behalf of the agent, not on behalf of the principals. And the agent is also liable for all expenses incurred for this Hajj, because the agent's act is contrary to the command; he was commanded to perform Hajj separately for each without combining. Preference cannot be given to one over the other because that would require a preponderant factor without evidence. Since the Hajj cannot be on behalf of both and neither can be given preference, it becomes on behalf of the agent. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Hajj 'an al-Ghayr, vol. 1 p. 317, Rahmaniyyah ed.: The case has three aspects: either he entered ihram for both together, or for one unspecified, or he made an absolute intention. If he intended both together — which is the case of the book — then he has opposed them because each of them commanded him to devote the Hajj exclusively for him and to intend it specifically at the time of ihram. If he did not do so, he became a violator, and it is not on behalf of either of them, since neither is more entitled than the other; so it occurs on behalf of the agent. It is not possible for him to assign it to one of them after that, because it has already occurred on his own behalf, so he cannot make it for someone else. Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Hajj 'an al-Ghayr, vol. 2 p. 86, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage introduces a legal maxim (qawida fiqhiyya) and applies it to a specific case in Hajj. The maxim: If a person commanded to do an act (the ma'mur) does it in a way contrary to the command (amr), the act is attributed to the ma'mur, not the commander (amir). This means the ma'mur bears the consequences and rewards, and the amir is not liable. The commentator then applies this to a case where two principals appoint one agent to perform Hajj separately for each. The agent, however, makes a single ihram intending to represent both. This violates the command because each principal required the agent to intend Hajj exclusively for him. Since the agent cannot give preference to one over the other without justification, and the act cannot be split, the Hajj is valid for the agent himself. He must bear the costs and the reward is for him. The text from al-Hidayah elaborates: there are three possibilities: ihram for both, for one unspecified, or absolute intention. In the case of intending both, it is a clear violation. The ruling is that the act is not for either principal, but for the agent. Once the act occurs for the agent, he cannot later assign it to another. This principle is widely applied in Hanafi fiqh, especially in matters of agency and vows.

Key Terms
المأمور (al-ma'mur): The person commanded to perform an act (agent/proxy).
الآمر (al-amir): The person who issues the command (principal).
المخالفة (al-mukhalafa): Contradiction of the command; acting contrary to the specific instruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two principals appoint an agent to perform Hajj separately, but the agent makes one intention for both, who is the Hajj valid for?
A) The first principal
B) The second principal
C) The agent
D) Both principals

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim: an agent's act contrary to command is attributed to the agent, not the principal.

Blood of Qiran and Tamattu' Is Thanksgiving, Not Penalty
Distinguishes dam of Qiran/Tamattu' from compensatory blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school classifies the dam of Qiran and Tamattu' as thanksgiving (shukr) rather than expiation, and apply this to determine liability in agency cases.

Core Idea
The dam of Qiran and Tamattu' is wajib as thanksgiving, not penalty; it falls on the actual performer, not the principal.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies a key distinction in the Hanafi school: the blood sacrifice required for Hajj al-Qiran and Hajj al-Tamattu' is not a penalty for a deficiency but a thank-offering for a blessing. This classification has practical implications, especially when one person performs Hajj on behalf of another. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assigning liability for the sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses the blood sacrifice (dam) required in Hajj al-Qiran and Hajj al-Tamattu'. The ruling is that this dam is wajib (obligatory), not as a penalty but as thanksgiving (shukr).
The term 'shukr' is central: it indicates gratitude for a blessing, not expiation for a shortcoming.
2
Understand the legal basis (talil)
The passage provides the rationale: the dam is due to the blessing of being able to combine two major acts of worship (Hajj and Umrah) in one journey. It is not a compensation for any failure. This is supported by the statement: 'وجب شكرا لما وفقه الله من الجمع من النسكين'.
The talil is based on the concept of gratitude for a divine favor.
3
Apply the ruling to agency
The passage then applies this principle to a scenario where a person commands another to perform Hajj al-Qiran. Since the dam is a thanksgiving for the actual act of combining, it becomes obligatory on the agent (the one who physically performs the rituals), not on the principal. The agent is the one who actually received the blessing of performance.
The principal only benefits legally (shar'an), but the actual deed is from the agent.

ترجمہ: دمِ قرآن اُس نعمت کا شکر ادا کرنے کے لئے واجب ہوا ہے جس کو اللہ تعالی نے دو عبادتوں کو جمع کرنے کی توفیق دی ہے۔

ترجمہ: حج تمتع اور قران کا دم، دم عبادت ہے، برخلاف باقی دموں کے کیونکہ وہ کفارات کے دم ہیں۔

Chapter: The Hady (sacrificial animal). (225) Indeed, the blood (sacrifice) of Qiran is obligated as thanksgiving for what Allah has granted him of combining the two rituals. Translation: The sacrificial blood of Qiran is obligated as a thanksgiving for the blessing that Allah has granted him to combine the two acts of worship. Explanation: The meaning of the above principle is that the blood of Qiran is not a compensatory blood (dam jabar), but a thank-offering. In Hajj al-Qiran, by Allah's grace, the servant performs both Hajj and Umrah together. This is a great blessing from Allah, and to give thanks for this blessing, a sacrificial blood is obligated. The author of al-Hidayah mentions this principle and explains that if a person commands another to perform Hajj al-Qiran, then in that case the blood becomes obligatory on the one who enters ihram (the agent), because the blood of Qiran is obligated as thanksgiving, and giving thanks is upon the one who performs the act, so the blood is also upon the one who enters ihram. (226) Indeed, the blood of Tamattu' and Qiran is a sacrificial blood (dam nusuk), unlike the rest of the bloods, for they are bloods of expiations (kaffarat). Translation: The blood of Tamattu' and Qiran is a blood of worship, contrary to other bloods because they are bloods of expiations. Explanation: The meaning of this principle is that the blood that comes in Hajj al-Tamattu' and Hajj al-Qiran is not due to expiation; rather it is dam nusuk, i.e., a blood of worship, because it is obligated as thanksgiving, as opposed to the blood of expiation and blood for violations (jinayat) which are compensatory bloods. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Hady, vol. 1 p. 320, Rahmaniyyah ed.: And the blood of Qiran is obligated on the agent because it is obligated as thanksgiving for what Allah has granted him of combining the two rituals. The agent is the one specifically receiving this blessing, because the actual act is from him, even though the Hajj occurs on behalf of the principal—because that is a legal occurrence, and the obligation of the thanksgiving blood is caused by the actual act emanating from the agent. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Hajj 'an al-Ghayr, vol. 3 p. 70, Dar al-Kitab al-Islami. Al-Hidayah, Kitab al-Hajj, Bab al-Hady, vol. 1 p. 320, Rahmaniyyah.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage clarifies the nature of the required sacrificial animal (dam) in Hajj al-Qiran and Hajj al-Tamattu'. It states two principles: first, the dam of Qiran is a thank-offering (shukr), not a penal or compensatory sacrifice (jabr). This is because the pilgrim has been granted the ability to combine two major acts of worship (Hajj and Umrah) in one journey, which is a special blessing. The thanksgiving obligation falls on the person who physically performs the act, i.e., the one who enters ihram. Second, the dam of both Qiran and Tamattu' is categorized as 'dam nusuk' (sacrificial blood of worship), in contrast to other obligatory blood sacrifices like those for violations (jinayat) or expiations (kaffarat), which are compensatory in nature. The commentator applies this to agency: if a person commands another to perform Hajj al-Qiran, the dam (sacrifice) is obligatory on the agent (the one who actually performs the rituals), not on the principal, because the actual act (the combining and the physical performance) is done by the agent. The principal only benefits legally (shar'an), but the thanksgiving is tied to the actual deed. This distinction affects liability for the cost and the ruling on validity.

Key Terms
دم القران (dam al-qiran): The sacrificial animal required for performing Hajj al-Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram).
دم المتعة (dam al-mut'ah): The sacrificial animal required for Hajj al-Tamattu' (performing Umrah first, then Hajj in the same year).
دم النسك (dam al-nusuk): A sacrificial animal offered as an act of worship, not for compensation or penalty.

Key Takeaway
The dam of Qiran and Tamattu' is wajib as a thank-offering for the blessing of combining rituals, and therefore it is owed by the actual performer, not the principal.

Dam al-Qiran is a Thank Offering, Not Compensation
Explains the legal principle that dam al-qiran is a thank-offering and its implication for deputized hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal principle of dam al-qiran as a thank-offering and apply it to determine who is obligated to offer the dam in a case of deputized Hajj.

Core Idea
Dam al-qiran is for the performer, not the commander — gratitude for the blessing of combining Hajj and Umrah.

In this passage, the Hidayah clarifies a key Hanafi rule: the sacrificial animal for Hajj al-Qiran is not a penalty but a thank-offering. Understanding this distinction determines who must slaughter the animal when one person performs the hajj on behalf of another. We will work through the reasoning that links the obligation to the actual performer.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its basis
Identify that the dam for Qiran is wajib as shukr (gratitude) for the blessing of combining the two rituals.
The text explicitly says: 'إِنَّ دَمَ الْقِرَانِ وَجَبَ شُكْرًا'.
2
Identify the reasoning (dalil aqli)
The obligation is tied to the actual performance because gratitude follows the action. The one who physically performs the combination is the recipient of the divine blessing.
The reasoning is rational based on the nature of shukr.
3
Apply to deputized hajj
If a commander (amir) hires a performer (ma'mur) to do Qiran, the dam is due from the ma'mur because he is the one who actually performed the rites.
The text: 'وَإِنَّمَا وَجَبَ دَمُ الْقِرَانِ عَلَى الْمَأْمُورِ'.
4
Distinguish from jibr (compensation)
Note that this differs from the Shafi'i view which considers dam al-qiran a compensation for omitting a separate Umrah. In the Hanafi school, it is purely a thank-offering.
This distinction affects who owes the dam in deputized cases.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the dam is on the ma'mur.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ دَمَ الْقِرَانِ وَجَبَ شُكْرًا لِمَا وَفَّقَهُ اللهُ مِنَ الْجَمْعِ مِنَ النُّسُكَيْنِ. وَإِنَّمَا وَجَبَ دَمُ الْقِرَانِ عَلَى الْمَأْمُورِ بِاعْتِبَارِ أَنَّهُ وَجَبَ شُكْرًا لِمَا وَفَّقَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ المُسكَيْن والمَأْمُورُ هُوَ الْمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ النِّعْمَةِ، لأنَّ حَقِيقَةَ الْفِعْلِ مِنْهُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ الْحَجُّ يَقَعُ عَنْ الْآمِرِ ، لأنَّهُ وُقُوعٌ شَرْعِيٌّ وَوُجُوبُ دَمِ الشُّكْرِ مُسَبَّبٌ عَنْ الْفِعْلِ الْحَقِيقِيِّ الصَّادِرِ مِنَ الْمَأْمُورِ.
Indeed, the blood of Qiran became obligatory as gratitude for what Allah granted him of combining the two rituals. And indeed the blood of Qiran becomes obligatory upon the commanded person considering that it became obligatory as gratitude for what Allah Almighty granted him of combining the two rituals, and the commanded person is the one specifically intended by this blessing, because the reality of the action comes from him, even if the Hajj falls for the commander, because it is a legal occurrence, and the obligation of the blood of gratitude is caused by the actual action performed by the commanded person.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage states the legal principle that the dam (sacrificial animal) required for Qiran Hajj is not a penalty but a thank-offering (shukr) for the blessing of being able to combine Hajj and Umrah. The author explains the consequence: if a person commands another to perform Qiran Hajj, the dam falls on the one who actually performs the rituals (the ma'mur), not the commander (the amir). This is because the dam is shukr for the actual act, and the actual act is done by the performer. Even though the reward of the Hajj goes to the commander (since it is a deputized act), the obligation of the dam is tied to the physical performance. This is supported by the quote from al-Bahr al-Raiq, which clarifies that the legal occurrence of Hajj on behalf of the commander does not transfer the obligation of the shukr dam because shukr is a result of the actual action.

Key Terms
دَمُ الْقِرَانِ (dam al-qiran): The sacrificial animal required for the one performing Hajj al-Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram).

Dam Nusuk vs Dam Kafarat in Hajj
Classification of Hajj sacrificial blood into nusuk and kafarat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between dam nusuk and dam kafarat in Hajj and explain the practical consequence regarding the timing of slaughter.

Core Idea
Tamattu' and Qiran require a worship sacrifice; all other Hajj blood is compensatory.

This lesson addresses a key classification in Hajj sacrifices. While many assume all Hajj blood is penal, the Hanafi school teaches that the dam for Tamattu' and Qiran is a special act of worship, not a penalty. Understanding this difference affects when and where the sacrifice must be performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
First, note that the dam in Hajj is divided into two types: dam nusuk (worship sacrifice) for Tamattu' and Qiran, and dam kafarat (compensatory blood) for everything else like jinayat and omissions.
2
Understand the basis of distinction
The distinction rests on the purpose: dam nusuk is a thank-offering for the blessing of combining Umrah and Hajj, while dam kafarat compensates for a deficiency or violation.
Shafi'i school classifies Tamattu' and Qiran blood as jibr (compensation), not pure worship.
3
Apply the timing rule
Because dam nusuk is an act of worship for a specific occasion, it must be slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr within the Haram. Other dam can be slaughtered at any time, though early is preferable to remove liability.
The rule ensures the worship sacrifice aligns with the festival of sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ دَمَ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ دَمُ نُسُكِ بِخِلَافِ بَقِيَّةِ الدِّمَاءِ فَإِنَّهَا دِمَاءُ الْكَفَّارَاتِ.
Indeed, the blood of Tamattu' and Qiran is a blood of worship, contrary to the rest of the blood, for they are bloods of expiation.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This principle classifies the dam (sacrificial blood) in Hajj. The dam required for Tamattu' (performing Umrah first then Hajj) and Qiran (combining both) is termed 'dam nusuk' (sacrifice of worship). This is because it is offered as a thank-offering for the blessing of being able to combine or perform the two acts. In contrast, all other types of dam in Hajj, such as dam al-jinaya (penalty for violating ihram) or dam al-kafarah (expiation for omissions), are classified as 'dam kafarat' (compensatory blood). This distinction has practical consequences: dam nusuk must be slaughtered specifically on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah) and within the Haram, while other types can be slaughtered at any time, though early slaughter is preferable to remove the liability quickly. The commentary elaborates that for non-nusuk blood, immediate slaughter is better because they compensate for a deficiency.

Key Terms
دَمُ نُسُكِ (dam nusuk): A sacrificial blood offered as an act of worship and thankfulness, not as compensation for a violation.
دَمُ الْكَفَّارَاتِ (dam al-kafarat): Sacrificial blood offered to compensate for a violation or omission during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the dam of Tamattu' is classified as what type of blood?
A) Dam kafarah
B) Dam jibr
C) Dam nusuk
D) Dam shukr

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' and Qiran demand a worship sacrifice (dam nusuk) with a fixed time, while all other Hajj blood is compensatory (dam kafarat) without a fixed time.
